Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And there should be between the two knives a finger's width of space, and then when you have marked both places, you place the hot iron on until it reaches the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and they should be spaced apart because they are not soldered by this cautery throughout; and that is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears from the eyes are descending from the veins that are on the top of the head, and medicine does not help, and you see the face of the patient turning red, and in his forehead there is pulsation like trembling; and if their eyes are sunken and moist so that the eyelashes have fallen off, and the eyelids are swollen and burned by the tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it in ancient times "cure contused", and it is that you do to the patient who has this disease, the hairs on his forehead, then make three cuts on the forehead evenly according to the length of the forehead; and let one of the cuts be as long as two fingers right in the middle of the forehead, going downward just above the nose, and the other two on either side of the temples, and be careful not to cut the arteries that are on either side of the temples; and keep your hand away from the jaw, and each wound should be about a finger's width apart, and have a sponge ready with some cloth to soak up the blood, then use the spatulum to apply the medicine to both sides where the headache is located:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision that is to be on the temple up to the second incision; and scorch all of the skin between the two incisions up to the sinus that is on top of the bone, then remove this spatula.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	if you put into the first incision the instrument that is called "cultellar", and it is very sharp on one side, and on the other side it is smooth and not at all sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the blade cutting towards the chest cavity, and the back of the blade towards the bone, and push it until it reaches the middle slit.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut through all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to what opens in the chest, and then make another cut in the middle slit to the other defier; and then draw out blood equally, and express the site for the extracted blood; then put into each slit a tent of old cotton, and place moistened drapes in wine and oil and garlic, and be careful that hot abscesses do not come to it; and on the third day loosen the ligature, and administer a large amount of cold water, then cure with basilicon ointment with rose oil, and other remedies for curing wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	from the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When one has an acute cataract that usually occurs, and you see the eyes thin and small, and weakened vision, and burnt eyelids; and the hair falls out, and in the head there is pain, and the patient sneezes; then from these signs you know that those matters and this cataract come from many veins, and the cure for it is to let it be, as it is.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to lean back his head, then make a large incision in the middle of the forehead, and another from the large eye socket.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves in the temples that control swallowing; and when the bone is exposed, soak up all the blood with a sponge, and then insert old cotton between the two lips of the incision and pack it with lint; then bind damp cloths soaked in wine and oil over it, and beware of hot abscesses; once it is removed, you should rub the bone until warm blood starts to flow, then treat it with astringent substances that promote clotting.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of flower of wheat and four parts of colophony, and make an ointment from it; and administer it to these wounds to dry up pus throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	the cleaning of ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: either grains or a stone or ore; or something flowing, like water and garlic and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it is stuck in the ear or another kind of object that does not adhere to or grow in the ear, put the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the stone, then distil a little oil of violets or oil of hellebore, and then administer extraction; and let him sneeze from scent, and plug his nostrils when he sneezes, and put pieces of cloth or wool around the ears, and prop the ears up on top.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	Many times it comes out through this treatment; and if it does not come out, then administer extraction with subtle pincers, whose form is thus:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it comes out with the pincers, that is good; if not, then bring about extraction with a fine needle of small wire; and if it does not come out in this way, then make a hook of bronze and insert the end of the hook into the hole of the ear firmly, and stop up what is around the hook with soft wax so that the air cannot enter with the hook; then pull it out forcefully, for very often it comes out as we have said. And if it does not come out in this manner, then take some glue from which birds are caught, and put into it some instrument that is appropriate for doing this, and place some cotton around it; then press the glue onto the pebble or whatever it is, and pull it out.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not come out from all these things that we have said, then you must hurry to split the ear so that the abscess and inflammation will come out, and the spasm; and the manner of the splitting is such that you first make the patient lean his head back, and draw blood according to the measure of its strength, then make the patient sit between your hands and turn his ear upward, and make a small split in the root of the ear at the fatty part from which it depends; and let the split be like a moon, so that you come to the pebble, then extract it according to your ability, and suck it strongly with your mouth; and treat it until it is healed.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre .i. spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is grain which is inside and it swells, then administer extraction; and if it cannot come out, then apply a thin spatula according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and make an incision on that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not do this when you think that the grains are moist from the moisture of the ear, until you have made many incisions; then extract it with subtle pincers and a suction cup, as we have said, so that the extraction is gentle.Si li estrazione de la piere ne soit fort dificile, si covient qu’il se fiet truchement de suc d’arbes qui soit aligeant a la piere, et que il ne blesse point le membre; car si il le blesse, li est a grant danger.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the earache therefore that is sharp in the ear, the patient should use sneezing of first-rate remedies, and fill the ear with soft cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And he should lie down on that same ear where the ache is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	if it jumps out because of this, that's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	if it does not, take many stones according to the size of your little finger, thin and light, and heat them in fire; then insert one into the ear and press down on it from above with another stone; and take another stone and press down on the stone that is in the ear; and continue to do this with one stone after another until all the ache comes out, and so it will all come out; and if you see any pus, take a straw, insert one end into the ear and heat the other end in fire until the most painful straw is burned; then do the same with another straw until all the ache is gone, as we have said for the stone.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of an insect, if it is a small body, like a flea or similar, treat it as we have said in the division section. But if it is a large body that can be felt, administer extraction with pincers; and this is the easiest thing to remove from the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of worms in the ears, when you treat it as we have said in the section on distillations, and the treatment does not help, then you should examine the ear in the sun; if there are any worms, pull them out with fine tweezers, and if they do not appear, take a cockerel's comb, from which is taken the dye:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And it is tight below and loose above.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And insert the thinnest end of the needle into the ear according to the amount of the suffering of the malady, then suck strongly on the cannula; do this repeatedly until all the pus comes out.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not come out, then plug the cannula with cotton as I have said for the stone; and if they do not come out as we have said, then administer distilling remedies that the ancients have experimented with for worm-cutting, and you will find them in the section on distilleries; and distill your oils and remedies into the ear through this instrument, whose form is as follows:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a .i. petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a .i. estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren .i. raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations .i. poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	And it is made of silver or brass with a narrow end and a wider top for distillation; and to press the distillation into the ear use an instrument of well-crafted brass, and if you wish, take a razor and wrap cotton around the blade; then pour your oil or juice, and whatever medicines you wish, into the cockerel's comb, and let the comb be in the ear; then insert the razor with all the cotton inside, and press your hand gently so that the oil is distilled into the ear canal; and the patient will feel it inside, and the distillation should be slightly warm as one heats it over the fire; and beware that it is not too cold, for the medicine would not then be so effective.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	the cleaning of ears
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient .i. poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without an eardrum; and the same thing happens to men through the cleaning of a wound, or from pus forming within the ear, and sometimes this cleaning reaches deep into the ear, so that one cannot see it; and sometimes there is only a little discharge, which can be seen clearly.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	Therefore, when it occurs deep within the ear and cannot be seen, it is a matter of painful healing in various conditions, and in this case, one should put the affected ear towards the sun; and look inside: if you see the membrane appearing, then it is working as it should.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And it should be sharp and smooth both in front and behind, so that it does not pierce the ear; if the membrane is due to pus or the body of the ear, then grab it with thin pins and gently scrape it, until all the pus is removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the growth is deep in the ear, take a thin, light scalpel and heat it slightly in the fire, then place it on the body of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the piercing pain that the patient feels on hearing, pierce gently, and be careful not to damage the nerves of the ear; then put a tent in the ear according to the size of the hole, and moisten it with Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do this every day until the wound is closed, then take a tent and moisten it in rose water, and sprinkle powdered vitriated copper on top; and if you see the ear swollen, then it is fitting to pull out the tent and insert another tent moistened with cerotum made of rose oil and wax, until the swelling is gone; then treat it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	And if bleeding occurs, immerse a sponge and cloth in cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other treatments that stop the bleeding that are used for distilling remedies.
de la char des papieres	of the charcoal of papers
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This poultice comes in papers from the herbs when they are moist and dry, so you should spread them with tongs and tweezers, and the top of a spatula from its roots; then put ground vitriol on the spot.
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without the outer skin, then cauterize with a lens subtlety, and the cautery after the incision is worth moving; and many times they return, as long as nothing remains of their roots; and when they are cauterized by fire, those roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of hail
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times there come on the ears things that look like gravel in their shape and hardness, and because of this the disease is called "hail", and it is a mass of moisture thick on top and bottom; the treatment is as follows: if the hail mutates from one side to another, and it is an easy thing to know, then open it with forceps, then peel off each layer gently, then take it with tweezers, and cut it out.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	if you cannot cut it out without piercing the membrane, do not trouble the patient at all; and if the split is large, sew it up with a stitch, and treat it until it heals; and if it is small, do not use force on it, for ointments will heal it immediately and prevent infection.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	And if the hematoma is descending into the ear towards the upper part, reverse the paper, and hold it with tweezers, and press from both sides; and if the paper is removed by the incision, that is not a problem; and when the hematoma is pressed, wash the eye with salted water, and cure the place of what exudes pus until the patient is healed.
de la graisse des eulz	of the fat of the eyes
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a fat that is woven into the webs of paper above, and this happens more to children than to anyone else, and it weighs heavily on themselves, and they get the catharsis in the mornings, and they cannot look at the light of the sun because their tears hasten to their own eyes; and because of this, they lie down on their faces, and sleep on top of them, and their papers are under their eyelids, moistening that which the inflammation and appearance have covered with exinach, which appears in the eye.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press the area between your fingers and feel the exinach coming out between them.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren .i. drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	And the manner of the operation is that the patient puts his head on the lap of the healthy person; and then take .i. linen cloth, and prepare a tent in the form of a circle according to the quantity that exinach contains in each part, and then put it over him; and press with your fingers from both sides, so that the exinach is gathered inside the circle. Then make an incision in the middle of the moistened spatumile, not any larger than the wound made in vein opening; and cut into the skin deeply enough so that you reach the exinach; and in various dispositions, exinach comes out of the incision, according to the shape of a piece of white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	Remove the bandage completely from one side between your fingers, and move your hand back and forth so that it is loose; and be careful not to push into the wound, otherwise you will reach all the way to the eye and cause bleeding.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	And if the wound opens at the beginning of the slit, gently open it slightly so that it appears; then remove it as we have said, then wet bandages in vinegar and water, place them on the area, and tie with a bandage.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	And if there are such men who grind salt and place it on to corrupt that moisture which remains.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the eye until it is healed.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes to that area, treat it with soothing poultices until it is healed.
des poilz des papieres	And if the pain is in the neck or mouth, then have the animal drink wine and brew, and apply apricot oil and powder to the area.
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs grow from papers unlike nature, and are enveillit, they harm themselves and bring on various diseases such as laments and the softening of papers and albugine, until it leads to their destruction; and there are four ways to treat this: by cautery with fire, or by medicine water according to what is before the cautery chapter, and it is done either by incision and sewing or by splints, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You should place the affected area in your dominant hand, then hold the paper of the eye with your left hand; if it turns, that's good, but if not, insert a needle with thread through it; and this should be done near the edge of the paper where the hairs are growing, and weave one thread throughout the entire paper, and then return it to the razing tool; next, make an incision in the area under the paper, under the abnormal hairs, all the way to the spatumile, cutting through the large and small larmier; then remove the thread and place a small tent of cotton and cloth under the paper, and sign a figure of enche on the paper, like a fuelle of mirte, and the shape should be according to the amount you see the paper rising.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If you have paper that is needed, cut it into a large amount according to how soft the paper is; then mark the entire spatumile along the two lines you have marked, and start from the larger one to the smaller; and let one of the slits be near the natural hair in the thickness of a root, then insert the needle into one of the two corners of the heart, then cut it all off; then bring the two lips together with a stitch of a thin woolen thread using an awl, and wipe away the blood, and dry the excess of the threads on the two sour eyes with any glue-like substance you see fit to use; if not, then don't worry about it, and leave the stitch and threads for three or four days; then cure the wound without stitches using dry and constricting substances, because the paper will lift up at the wound's souding and joining, but the stitch is painful (as the ancients say), and this work causes no fear; there is another way: you mark the paper in a shape like the leaf of a myrtle tree, as we have described, with three slits spaced according to the form that is shown here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	then cut out what is on top with small scissors evenly according to the form which is here:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you cannot hold the tongs, and the object is not even, then take a needle with some thread, and insert it into the wound; and take another thread next to the large blood vessel, and the second thread next to the small one, and bring the threads together between your fingers evenly; then lift your hand evenly, and lift all the skin on which you have made the sign, as we have described, then bring the two lips of the wound together with stitches, and heal it until it is cured; and if an abscess comes to your incision, calm it with cerotic ointment and similar soothing ointments; and sometimes the hairs of the paper are converted: so you should use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching on both sides is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The treatment of the bones is as follows: you must turn over the parchment and put it inside according to what I have said, and then make two bones by art, and two thin ligatures as long as the parchment and the width of the spine; and cut two heads into two parts where you hold the threads; then assemble them both subtly above what is on top of the parchment of the eye, and strain the two bones out of their two formed parts; and leave it like this for some days, and the skin that was strained will die and harden and fall off as it drops by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it persists and the wound has strength, then heal it until it is cured; and when the wound is closed, and the paper is raised, and the hairs no longer hurt; and this is the form of the two cannings that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The procedures are such that you pierce a fine needle and thread in with a thin, soft silk thread; then assemble the heads and tie them together subtly, and let the length of the threads be about a palm long; then arrange another thin silk thread in the case, and tie the end of the thread; then put the patient's head in your hand; and have it exposed to sunlight so that the procedures are declared, for this is a subtle and fine procedure, then pierce the needle through the parchment directly onto the hair, drawing it up through the parchment until it reaches the case, and thread that hair into the case, whether there is one or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand so that the hairs come out straight through the case with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	And if the hunt is treated and the hair does not come out with it, then you will treat the hunt from below to the very thread that you ordered for it, until the hunt comes out through the hole above and you see it with your eye; then you will pull the hunt and the thread, and close the eye and leave it closed for 1 or 2 days, until the hair grows back in its place and the flesh grows over it; and if the hair is short, accompany one long hair from the horse's tail, and let it grow with that one, until it is elongated and then you release it.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the pustule of the eye
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease called "alacrity" or warts comes in the eye, there are two ways it occurs: one natural and the other unnatural.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And it happens suddenly from a wound, or from cutting or cauterizing, and in similar ways.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way to treat it is that you split the ulcer, and loosen the edges of it, and place within it tents made of linen, and dress it until it is healed; and one must not use in its treatment anything that would dry it out or constrict it.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do that, the disease will return worse than before; but one should use softening things, such as fenugreek; and rosewater or water made alcoholic with honey, and seeds of flax cooked in it, and ointments of aquilone softened in some of the oils, and one should wrap a tent around it, and dress it thus.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the goal of your treatment is that you take care not to let it heal according to its previous form; and these works that we have described are remedies for this disease so that it does not return to its previous form.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	of the pus that comes in the eye
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease, which is beneath that which is truly called "axacrati", is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	Accidents come from wounds and incisions and cauterization and similar things; the way to treat them is to take a needle with a double thread, pierce it into the flesh, and make it go through from one armpit to the other so that the threads come out on both sides of the body. Then, the flesh above the needle is lifted up to the shoulder blade, and the cup is placed over the armpit widely.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the shape of the wound returns as it should, that is good; but if not, then take a razor and put it in the incision, and turn the wound over, and make two incisions along the edge inside the wound; and let the two corners of the incisions be on either side of the incision you have made, and form angles so that when they are brought together, the shape is like that of the letter "Y" in the German alphabet; then remove the flesh, according to the quantity that is attached under the wound, from that which follows the wound, and then join the two severed parts and sew them with a thread of wool; then treat it as we have said, with softening medicines and bandages, until it heals.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the disease comes from a split or stitch or cautery, then you should make a clean split under the hairs of the scalp, and according to what is mentioned above; then unsheathe between the two lips of a tent, as I have said; and one must perform the operation according to the form of the disease, for it is very diverse in form, and the wise master prepares remedies with all his power so that he makes the figure return to its natural form; and the patient himself, according to what he needs in terms of treatment and instruments in various dispositions.
dou soudement de la papiere	And suddenly from the scalp
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this soudure occurs in a similar manner to that of the scalp, with the paper above being separated from the white of the eye, and unable to move or perform its natural functions, then you must therefore pierce the point of a razor under the paper and lift it up; and press it with tweezers until you grab what is open in the sphynctered subtile, which is neither too sharp nor too trench-like, so that the patient cannot bear the pain of the sphyncter being too sharp and bleeding the eye; and make your incision to peel off this union lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural form; and when all of this assembly is healed, they sometimes have watery eyes with a saline solution, and the eye is raised with soft wool; then put a tent made of linen between the paper and the eye, and place moistened wool on top of the eye; and after the third day, use the collyrium and soothing remedies until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	of the eyelid
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	You should know that there are two types of nail: one is nervy and resembles a hard wart; the other is not nervy but resembles white congealed moisture, which, when touched with iron and pinched as though to break it, cannot be broken by anyone. Both types originate near the inner corner of the eye and grow little by little until they cover the entire eyelid and obscure all light and movement of the eye.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of incision is that the patient should place his head in your lap, then open his eyes; hold the piece of paper in your hand, then grip the nail with small forceps and lift it up; next, take a needle, thread a horsehair, or cow's hair, or bull's hair through it, and double over the tip of the needle a little and insert it into the nail, then tie the nail with a thread and lift it up, and scrape along the side of the nail where the eyelid follows the tear duct down to the lash line, then cut the remaining portion at the root of the tear duct, carefully and with small forces, until you reach the delicate sphincter; leave the natural tissue of the tear duct alone so that no incision comes near it. Sometimes only the nail at the inner corner needs to be lifted and tied as described above; then scrape all around the sphincter, for this is where the form lies:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And be careful not to touch and break the fleshy membrane, or pierce the eyelid; after the incision, drop a little crushed vitriol into the eye, and place a collar of litarge around the eye, leaving it on until the next day; then treat the eye as needed until it heals.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	If the nail is not sensitive and you cannot pierce it with a needle, and the hook cannot enter, this nail-like appearance is often cured by medicine; and it grows back as I have described in the section on division. And if you see it covered, then treat the eye of the patient, and take the spatulum, a small and sharp tool, according to this shape:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And lift the nail gently, and if you see that it does not thin out and the cuticle recedes, then drop a collar made of litarge and red copper and ground seal from your mouth into the eye; then stop up the eye until the next day. Then the next day, repeat the other procedure according to this same method, until it is all removed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is contrary in the eye, as with a hot abscess, then milk it, and first treat the hot abscess until it is healed, then repeat the procedure as before, until it is healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the eyelid causes great harm in the eye, then pierce it with an awl and scoop out a portion but not all of it, so that the body of tears does not enter; then drop into the eye a red collar made from litarge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the flesh that grows over the pupil
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	In some men's eyes, a red blister sometimes forms, covering the eyeball and constricting it under the eyelids, resembling a rose on a wall; the patient then puts his head down to you, after which you work on the eye, and with all that heat, you push the flesh towards the nails, holding it there with force; then cut into the first blister, and continue cutting all the way to the root, being careful not to hurt the eye during the procedure; the incision should be made as we described in the section on finger incisions, using gentle forces to remove the nail, as demonstrated in this chapter; when the incision is complete and all the flesh has been removed, apply seal oil or similar corrosive medicines, and put cotton wetted with egg white over the eye to prevent a hot abscess from forming; if nothing remains, and the white of the eye turns red, indicating a hot abscess, then leave the eye alone and treat the abscess with soothing remedies for hot abscesses; then return to your work until it is healed, and likewise, do this for any blisters that form on the eye in this manner.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, you should adapt the treatment to each weak eye according to its natural condition; and for accidental conditions, use an iron instrument in your treatment; and do not insert your finger into any of these treatments until you see that this member can bear that treatment.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of them
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	Such are red veins that are covered over the eye, and obscure its sight and weaken the eye all day.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, first, you must examine the eye to see if it has any other disease besides the red veins; then treat it in this manner: instruct the patient to rest his head in your lap, then press those veins gently all around according to your wisdom, and let the pressings be subtle twice according to this form.
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be two folds by degrees in one body according to this shape:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then press those veins gently, and draw out the blood drop by drop after each other, until you see the veins removed from the eye; and be careful not to pierce the eye with the tips of the spatulae, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very skillful in your work so that you do not touch anything but the veins; and when you have done this, distil into the eye green and red collyrium to corrupt what remains of the cyst.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot collect all that in that hour, then make a poultice of things soothing the pain of the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain is eased and there is a warm abscess, then begin again according to this method that is before until it is healed; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	of the eye fistula
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	Examine the 'arissati' fistula closely: when you heal it with cautery and hot medicine according to what I have said before, and it is not healed, there is a hole in it where you must cut into the abscess, removing all the moisture until the bone is exposed.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is exposed and you see corruption and blackness, then there is the cause of this malady; it is called  'aspre chief'  and should be treated by making an incision from one side to the other, puncturing like a file as shown in the present figure.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place it over the site of the corrupt bone, then turn it between your fingers and press your hand a little while you know that the corruption is gone; and do this several times, then restore the site with drying medicines.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the place is swollen and pus forms and the body of the fistula is swollen and remains that way for 40 days without healing and no bad accident occurs, then you can be sure it is healed; if not, there is another method to bring the fistula to a hole in the nose according to this form: you must uncover the bone with iron a second time and with sharp medicines, and when it is uncovered, grab it with forceps according to this form, and let the head of the iron be three-pronged, and let the shaft be tapered down to the tip as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	then he places it on the bone below the eyeball, and moves his hand away from the eye a little, then returns to press the needle all the way through the bone until he feels the patient's pulse through the bone if he keeps his hand on his wrist; then he should apply dry medicine as I have taught you, and when the flesh heals and hardens, he should examine the wound; then it is lighter for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the exit of the eye
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the eyes open fully all around and there is no disturbance to the brain or thinning, then you should ligature the patient; then treat the eye, then place cups or suckers without piercing to draw out, then apply a poultice over the eye made of acacia and aloe and incense and myrrh, and then bind the eye tightly with bandages and clothes; and the manner of the clothes is that you take quite soft clothes, double each in four, and then place one upon another according to the quantity that the eye needs; then tighten it from above with a hard bandage, and repeat the cups to draw out without piercing; then remove the cups and leave the eye tightened day and night, and if the ligature softens, you should tighten it greatly; then remove the ligature after a day and a night, and if you see the eye healing, that is good; if not, then restart the poultice and the clothes and the ligature and the cups until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	from the bursting of a web
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disruptions come in the woven web, then it opens and comes out of the papers like a grain of resin, and is terrible to see; therefore, if you see it covered, the work is such that you push a needle into the root of the part underneath up to the part above, then push another needle where there is a double thread in the part of the eye; and pierce it, and leave the first needle according to its position; then cover the place of the double thread and tie one part of the web around, and tighten it well, then remove the needle and put a soft lamb's wool on top; and let it be until the threads break with the membrane, then cure the eye with comforting things until the wound is healed; and sometimes the wound is restrained by the web in each part by a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the eyes cause much distress, pierce them with a sharp spatule that comes from the bottom of the eye, and dry the white moisture and lower the eyes, and enter in at once; then pull until they are healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the bottom of the eye
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is nothing other than a tumor which is assembled in the eye, resembling descending water, but it is not water; and the manner of its appearance in the treatment is that you make the patient sit on a prepared and straight seat, then hold his head between your hands from both sides, and move it until you see the tumor come up to your eyes; then it should be punctured, and the light should be blocked so that the patient can see things as he used to; and if it does not go down below, know that it is a tumor, but if the swelling of the tumor is not apparent as we have said,
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the spatulum and gently pry up the conjunctiva from the cornea and the cornea itself, until the membrane is loosened; and when it has been released, distill into the eye hot water mixed with honey, or water in which fenugreek and honey have been boiled, and then treat it further until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	of the eye waters
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have already discussed the appearance of the diseases in this section and what should be done to pierce them; now act according to these instructions for the sake of health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You should make the patient sit between your crossed hands, away from the light of the sun, and squeeze the healthy eye firmly; then place the paper of the eye in your left hand if the eyes are on the left, or in your right hand if they are on the right; then take in your right hand, if the eyes are on the left, the instrument called "almagda," or in your left hand if they are on the right; then place the tip of the instrument along the edge of the cornea through the white part of the eye to the edge of the lower eyelid, and press the instrument gently, and turn your hand so that almagda pierces through the white part of the eye, and you will feel that almagda reaches the empty space; and the depth of the channel of almagda should be equal to the thickness of a prune from the edge of the blackness; this is the cornea of the eye; then you will see the bone in the paper due to the clarity of the corneal membrane, and then push the instrument down to where the water is, then express it under one channel after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	if the water now runs down, then let the patient see the instrument in front of him and look at it.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and if the water flows back up the second way, push it out with the instrument, and when it is lodged and does not flow upwards again, gently extract the alma-guda by twisting your hand a little; then put some gem-stone powder into the eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then apply to the eye a sponge or lamb's wool soaked in rose oil and abundant egg white, and bind it up with clean cloth.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	We, and those of our time, put on powdered comfrey mixed with abundant egg white.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if almagda cannot enter the eye due to its hardness, because there are some people whose eyes are too hard, then you should take the instrument called  "alberit", of which this is the shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so, piercing only the conjunctiva, and not going too deep, but making the incision subtle; then put in the alma-guda as we have said; and when the treatment is complete, prepare for the patient a dark sleeping place where he sleeps on his back in a dimly lit room; and he should be free of all movement, and eat light foods, and not move his head to the right or left, and he should be bound according to his condition for three days; then untie him in that same dimly lit house, and test his vision, and let him see some things, and then put on the bandage again until the seventh day; and you should not do this during the hour of the treatment or after the incision now, but you should ease it so that the water rises gently.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	if such an abscess comes, you should loosen the eye before the seventh day, and apply what soothes the abscess; and when it is soothed, then loosen the eyelid and put a gold ring over it to cover the eye, and let him remain in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then exit the house little by little, and return to his own house; and know that no disciple should intervene in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from Persia, who told us that in his country they pierce with alum, causing water to flow out, but I have never seen anyone doing this in our land, nor have I read of it in any books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the forms of almagda, because those who do not know them will see them; and they should be made of brass properly:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And the tips of these pliers should be of the same subtlety, and the handles in .iij. angles bent.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart above the chest
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Sometimes there are born or are found horses with diverse deformities, from which some seem like scorpions with many feet; and there are others with hooves of a dark color, and also hoofless ones with good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	With those of these horses that are hoofless and not deformed, you should make the patient sit in your lap facing the sun; open his nostrils, and pour something into the horse's nose and lead him away; then hold what you can reach with a very subtle, pointed instrument until you know that the horse has been completely cured.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	And if anything remains which one cannot cover, then open it with one of the subtle instruments lightly so that nothing remains; and if without swelling, or an abscess occurs, then lances it as it should be; and if they are malignant abscesses, then hasten to cauterize them until the pus is stanched and all the corruption is removed, then pour in wine or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If it works and moisture comes up to the palate, you know that it is healthy; and if the moisture does not penetrate as it should, you know that there is rotten meat in the bone above, because the instruments do not come to cut: therefore you must put a piece of linen thread, quite thick, through the nose, and let it hang down with a nodule at each end, about an inch or less between each; and the patient holds the end of the thread in his mouth as far back as he can, and pulls it through until it comes out of the nose; and children often do this at school, and it is easy for anyone who wants to do it; then hold one end, which comes out of the nose, in one hand, and the other end, which comes out of the mouth, in the other hand, and draw them both gently while you feel the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Do this as long as you know that the nails have corrupted the flesh, then pull the nail, wash the blood, and moisten the nail in Egyptian ointment, and put it back into the nose as before; do this for three days or more, until the ointments corroses all that is left of the flesh; and then put a plug of lead in the nose for a few days until it heals, and if it needs dry medicines, use them; and this is the form of the instrument to cleanse the head, with which one distils oils and medicines into the nose:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	It should be made of silver or bronze, resembling an open lamp, like a tube, and the instruments should be inserted into it; and if you wish, make a closed tube, and fill it with medicine to cleanse the nose; and there should be a handle on the instrument to hold it while heating the oil or any other liquid.
de la char sor le neis	of the heart above the chest
