Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times a disease called "telul" arises at the top of the head, and it grows and becomes great sores, so much so that it is visible to the eye; therefore, you should cut it at the beginning, and remove all the pus, then place the cautery or burning medicine on it; and if one delays cutting it until it becomes large, take heed whether it is hard, of a dark color, and lacking in feeling: do not touch it with iron, for it is an abscess, and when one cuts it, great harm comes to the patient. And if the abscess is due to pressure rather than a dark color, and you see that one can cut it all away, then drain the patient and cut it without fear, and clean the area of dry, constricting substances.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the nose has been cut and sewn
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Know that when solution of continuity occurs in one of these cartilage structures, it benefits few people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, when this happens to someone, look to see if the wound is fresh with all its blood; and then attach the two lips together with a stitch, then heal it; and if the lips are separated on both sides, you should scorch all parts of their skin until they heal, then sew the two lips together, and apply powder upon powder of dragon's blood, and ground incense; and place an ointment of strong or other binding ointment over the powders, and let it heal by itself, then cleanse it with ointment.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The method of sewing is that you assemble the solution: either with needles, as we have said in sewing the belly; or with thread, as I have told you before.
des apostemes des levres	of abscesses on the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the mouth there are hard abscesses inside the lips, similar to grains of wheat, both smaller and larger; therefore, you should split the lips, cut into each node, and squeeze it in every part; then apply vitriol powder after incision, until the blood is stanched; then use a poultice of garlic, and clean the area with dry things until it heals.
de la char des gencives	of gum bleeding
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times a growth arises on the gums, which the ancients call "albus". You should hold it with tweezers and cut at its root, letting the pus or blood flow; then place powdered vitriol or other drying and constricting powders over the wound. If the growth returns after the incision, and this often happens, cut it again and cauterize it; if it does not return after cauterization, that is how you treat an abscess.
des sordens	from sorens
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes they are gathered at the top of the teeth inside the mouth between the gums, and there are ugly and rough growths; sometimes the teeth are black, yellow, or green, indicating that corruption has reached the gum, and they smell bad; so you should have the patient hold his head in your hands, and press his teeth so that they are exposed, until nothing remains; and in this way, deal with blackness, yellowness, and other discoloration, until they are cleaned. If what is removed at first bleeding is good, it's fine; if not, then do it again the next day and the third day, until everything is removed. And know that teeth need different forms of instruments to clean them according to what their condition shows, so that the scaler with which one cleans between the teeth has other forms than those with which one cleans the tops of the teeth; and these forms and others should be prepared for you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	When you treat a toothache, it is important to wait as long as possible before pulling the tooth, because it is a very serious matter and one should have no excuse for not treating it properly.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Then, when the patient is forced to pull, you must be certain of the tooth that is causing the pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain deceives the patient, and he believes it is in a sound tooth, and pulls out the good tooth; and still the pain does not go away because of this, as long as the evil tooth remains, for we have already tried this with these healers; and when you are certain of the tooth that causes the pain, you must scrape around the tooth all around with a strong spatula to push back the gum on all sides; then he pulls it with his fingers or with fine tweezers, little by little, until it is well loosened, then he firmly holds the tweezers and the patient's jaw in your lap, so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After that, pull out the tooth carefully without breaking it, and if it will not come out, take one of these instruments and insert it into each side gently, then move it as you did before.And when it is extracted, it is necessary to stop the bleeding with a sponge, and to apply a poultice made of egg white, honey, and rose water over the wound, and to bind it tightly with a bandage.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are pierced and eaten, then you must fill the holes with pieces of cloth; and then gently pull them with tweezers so they do not break on being pulled; and one must work very gently around the gum to loosen the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be careful that you do not break it and leave a part of it behind, for then the illness will return with greater pain due to the root's maliciousness.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And beware of doing as ignorant surgeons do, who in their haste and audacity sometimes break the tooth, and don't follow our advice; but sometimes they bring about great illness due to the roots that remain, or because they break the tooth, as we have often seen. And when the tooth is pulled, wash the place with wine or garlic and salt; and if bleeding occurs, which often happens, apply powdered vitriol to the site; and if that doesn't work, cauterize it.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shape of the instruments, which are mute when hitting teeth first, should have long points and thick handles so that they do not bend when you hit the tooth; these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be made of thick, well-made iron, and have teeth to hold the mucus.
de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains in the tract, you should put wet cotton soaked in butter over it for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	until the area is softened; then insert the tweezers called "algefri", which make the shoulder look like a sick bird's beak; and inside, they are shaped like a file, and that is their form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots will not come out with these tweezers, you must uncover the flesh all around the root and place the instrument called "althali", which is to say, tongs, of which this is the form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be strong and thick so that it does not break, and if the root slips out through this, that is good; if not, then use all the instruments, of which the forms come below:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one should use this instrument which has two branches, of which this is the form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments which are in the reason of the teeth, and of this instrument which looks like large tweezers, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	Let this instrument be outside so that it cannot break, and know that there are many dental instruments; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise master finds by himself his instrument according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are many diseases in which the ancients did not teach any instrument because of their diversity. And if it does not break or pierce the bone, but protrudes, then he seeks the instruments that he needs, as I have told you, and helps with gestures, from which this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and strong enough to hold the bone so that it doesn't slip, but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines. And if there is a protrusion in the bone, and it is small, then cut it out with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When a tooth appears not according to the natural order of the body, and its shape is ugly, especially in virgin women, then you should know whether the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or ground down. Then pull it out; and if there is pus with the tooth, then take this instrument whose form is like a small beak, and let it be made of iron with a sharp edge on its end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And push it in and out gently due to the hardness of the tooth, and so that you do not move the others. And if it is apparent that it can be filed, then file it with a special file as shown in the form:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and it is like the file with which needles are made; and gently file the tooth a little at a time by hand, so that it does not move until it chips; then smooth it completely at the end with a file, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, one should file down the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth is loosened by either percussion or biting down, and the patient cannot press on what he is eating without defecating, and you have treated them with constricting remedies which do not work, then they should be restrained with a gold wire, because silver wires turn green and rust, but gold never moves; and the wire should be neither too thin nor too thick, according to the amount of space between the teeth. And if you see the teeth tilting, take the wire and wrap it twice around the two healthy teeth, then put the shoulder joint in between the teeth, whether there is one or more of them, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin the cover again as far as where you started, and gently tighten your hand until there is bleeding, so that it does not move. And the gold wire should be placed at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then pull the teeth of the thread with a pair of tweezers, and bring them together, and press them between the healthy teeth, and place it so that it does not cut the tongue; then leave it tight as long as it can stay, and if it slips or the threads break, then hold it in place with another thread; let it remain and serve like this for all its time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two bad ones, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is put back in its place, little by little, as we have said; and only a wise and experienced person should do this, because sometimes the shape of a tooth is made from cow bone, and put in where the defect is, and tied as we have said, and it remains and serves like this for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the wound of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes this ligament, which comes under the tongue by nature, is born like that; or it can be caused by an accident from a wound; and the treatment is such that you open the mouth of the patient, and hold his head in your healthy hand, and lift up his tongue; then grab the thick nervous ligament so that the tongue is separated from its place, and if there is hardness or a knot, it is due to a sudden wound, then cut it with scissors; and be careful that the incision is not too deep, because of the artery that is underneath; and when you have finished, raise the hand with water and garlic, or cold water, then place a tent of linen under the tongue; and every night, tie the patient's tongue so that it does not adhere.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if bleeding occurs, apply powdered vitriol to the area; and if the blood clogs, cauterize with a lentigo cautery, which is good for this. Then treat it further until it is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it discolored, black, or hardened, and the patient does not feel any pain, then do not touch it, as it is a ulcer; and if it is leaning towards a blister and there is moisture, apply the unguent of spathumile subtil and drain it from both sides. If blood oozes out during your treatment, apply vitriol until it dries up, then return to your treatment until you draw out all the pus. Afterwards, wash the area with water and soap, and treat it further until it is completely healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there occur in the throat ulcers called "godath", and they are properly called almonds; when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they do not heal, then take heed: if they are hard abscesses of small size and a light color, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is thick, do not touch it with iron, also for fear of bleeding; but let it be until it is dead, and then you will burst it, or it will break by itself; and if it is of a white color and the root is thin, have an instrument to cover it, but first look to see if the abscess is calm and pacified.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the patient sit facing the sun, and his head in your lap, and open his mouth and hold his tongue between your fingers, and press it down to the root of the instrument, with which you will make the shape; and let it be of fine silver or brass as thin as a knife.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	While pressing the tongue against the instrument, you will see the abscess; take the hook and insert it into the almond, pulling it upwards as hard as you can. Bring out any pus with it, then scrape the instrument against the abscess again, so that it forms a point; this is how it should look, like a sharp spike. The head of the instrument should be curved, one end curved in one direction and the other in the opposite direction, very thin, and made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, you can use tongs, shaped like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And let it be sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, cut the other according to the same method, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, and water and garlic, and if bleeding occurs, gargle the patient with water, or with peels of pomegranates that have been cooked, or with myrtle leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses besides the two tonsils develop in the throat, so cut them then as you did the two tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	I treated a woman for an abscess that was deep inside her throat, specifically, it was a small, but very sensitive abscess; and the whole throat was swollen closed so the woman could not breathe through the windpipe which was blocked by the swelling, nor eat or drink, and she would have died if it continued like this for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had grown so much that it had forced its way out through the two openings of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I quickly cut into one of the openings in her nose then pulled the pus out and cleared a large portion of it; I then cut into the other opening in her nose and cleared that too, then opened up her mouth and pressed her tongue down to the root of the instrument with which I was cutting. Then I cut into the abscess again and scooped out part of it, but only a little blood came out. So the windpipe in her throat was cleared and she could drink water and wine, and I continued to cut into that abscess for a long time; and the abscess would grow again and fill up the space I had emptied, so much so that it became very large; then I packed it with a poultice and cauterized it inside her throat. In this way it stopped growing. And I left these parts and did not hear of her after me.
de l’uve	of the liver
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When swelling descends to the eye, and it is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is swollen and round below, it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the abscess is eased, and it is subtle; and if it is round and not long, and it is blood-red or a fuschia color or black, then you should avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it according to the manner that I have described, of its white and length, you should have the patient sit facing the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument which we have mentioned earlier; then insert the needle into the eye, and draw it out from below, and scoop it with one of the two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you should not cover anything more than the superfluity that is beyond the natural term; for if you cover more, it weighs on the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two testicles, and heal until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear from covering, then you should use the cautery of the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery is for hot agaric.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of the cautery is for the hot agaric. And it is that the patient puts his head in yours, and then presses his tongue against the instrument that we have described in the chapter on cauterization, and dissolves with strong water, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and use the application of this instrument, from which comes the shape:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has a stem at its tip where the medicine is placed, like the handle of a spoon, and you place the instrument with all the medicine on top of the eye; and the patient should lie on his side so that the saliva and mucus from the medicine flow out of his mouth and do not go down his throat and into his lungs. Then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it become soft and the sting of the medicine lessen. And if you see it, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and wet the cotton in the medicine, and insert the instrument completely into the cotton on top, so that the cotton sticks to the eye; and do this often until the cautery is complete, then leave it to dry and fall off after four or five days. And if you need to reapply the cautery, do so, and afterwards wash the area around the medicine with cotton dipped in butter, and cleanse what is around the medicine; and use rose water, and treat it with gargles until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision or cautery; if it is treated by fumigation in this way, take calamin, hyssop, oregano, rue, chamomile, avens, and similar herbs, and mix them all or some of them in a pot, and add garlic, and let it boil. And the pot should be well glued with strong clay, and in the pot there is an instrument shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	Whether made of silver or bronze, place one of the tools in the mouth of the patient so that the vapors rise to the eye through the canal, until the eye is numbed; then repeat often, until the eye dries out. Be careful not to do this at the beginning of a hot abscess, as many things can go wrong; and do not do it after the hot abscess has subsided.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not available, take a straw and place an egg yolk in the end, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the egg yolk does not allow the vapors to harm the mouth, and it is a beneficial remedy together.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a bone or fish spine, or some other thing gets stuck in the throat; so you must pull out what you can see and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you can move the object; and if it does not appear to you and is lodged in the throat, you must make the patient vomit so that the meat is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the thing will come out through vomiting. Or the patient may swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it comes to the place, it will get stuck, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out in the way we have said, take an instrument of salt plaster according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the instrument be curved at the end so that it can enter the throat more easily, and let the head be raised upwards; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, lest it be broken, nor push the bone in; and move so that the patient swallows the instrument, so that he is moved where the object is lodged; then he swallows it, or you pull it out with the instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the blood from the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the blood is bled, as I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when this does not help, then look into the throat of the patient towards the sun, then press his tongue with the tool that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see blood, draw it out with a tiny hook, or with fine tweezers that are suitable for this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	If this doesn't work, take a small horsehair and put it in the wound, then heat the hair with hot iron, and do this repeatedly.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a fever all day:
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	then take a full glass of cold water, open the mouth and pour it in without swallowing, and move it around with their hand frequently; as soon as the blood touches the water, it will stop.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it doesn't stop as we have said, then smoke the patient with assafetida, using the instrument I described for smoking out the eye; do this many times, because it will stop without bleeding.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way to do the smoking is to take a pot with burning charcoal in it, and place over it a lid with a hole in the middle, and put the end of the instrument into that hole; then smoke out the patient, and have the patient put their head in their mouth, and close their mouth so the smoke doesn't escape, but comes to the blood; and the blood will stop now, and if it doesn't stop, then repeat the smoking many times; and let the patient be thirsty, and eat salty and sour things, and don't drink water; and then it will come out through this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument with which one draws out the blood is, when one can see it, like curved tweezers so that they can enter the throat; and it has a shape like a surgeon's forceps, and it has roughness from limed iron, so that it cannot let go of what it grabs; and see here the shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	There are many types of abscesses, according to what the memories that come later in this book from one and another, and they differ in penetration and size; and there are two kinds, one in its appearance itself, and in what it holds moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second kind is because of the places where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the fundament, and the abscesses of fleshy places are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in practice.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And in some abscesses one must not pierce until the bowels are cooled according to their completion; and there are others that one must pierce when they have become crusty, and they do not die according to their completion, like abscesses that are near joints.Et li apostemes qui sont en les joinctures de la char, si convient a percier quant il sont crut, et ne doivent mie tant que il soit meure; car li bowe n’est mie frois tant que il ne soit crut, ains est chauf et corant, si qu’il ne doit mie estre percier tant que il ne soit crut.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when an abscess occurs near the joints and is left until it becomes pus-filled around the edge, by chance the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, which causes contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or, if the abscess is near the principal limb and you delay piercing it until it becomes pus-filled, it will harm the principal limb. If it is near the fundament, one should pierce it so that it may drain; but one must not pierce an abscess without digestion being complete except for the one which is by the fundament, lest it fester inside and become elongated, and a fistula develop, taking a long time to heal.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And one should know the time of piercing an abscess that is mature according to its completion, which is when the pain subsides, the fever decreases, and there is a reduction in swelling, redness, discharge, and discomfort at the apex of the abscess, along with other signs. The piercing should be done at the highest point of the abscess, where there is movement and an opening; it should be pierced from the length of the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints affecting nerves and arteries, and in all similar locations without fold or crevice.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	These are bent according to the limb they affect.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when an abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to let the piercing wait until digestion is complete, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, the body will be harmed and filled with filth from it, and perhaps the lips and the depths of it will harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is an abscess that should be punctured according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must treat small abscesses with small incisions; and large abscesses, large ones, and many incisions according to the appearance of their size; and for such abscesses where one should cut out the core, and cover it up: when they have become like pieces of cloth, and are deadened, then one must do as one does with blisters: and there are some with three angles, and some which one covers like the fuel of myrrh, that is, abscesses of the fingernails; and there are some where one makes a round incision, and other incisions, and similar coverings.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, like a superficial boil, you must pierce it plainly; and when the boil is large and has drawn a great blister, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the blister in one hour, but some part of it; then stop the boil until the next day, then draw out something again; do this several times from great to small, until the blister is all out; likewise if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman carrying a child, or a young child, or an old decrepit man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pus sometimes erupts with the blister, which may kill the patient without you realizing it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Avoid this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced your boil, wash the wound, and look if the wound of the boil is small; and if it is a plain cut, apply tenters made of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large boil with many openings, you should place a tent in each opening so that they press against one another; and if you have cut into the boil a part of the skin, and you have pulled it back, then fill it with old dry cotton or rags of linen without moisture, and let it stay for three days; then remove it, and treat the wound with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if you experience bleeding from your work, bring cold water and ease, and wet the cloth, and place it over the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, bring management and treatment, and the powders that I have described earlier in this book; and if it is during winter, and the area is very nervous, then you should place wet tents and clothes soaked in warm wine and oil; and if it is in summer, and the area is fleshy, then you should place wet clothes soaked in water and oil, or in cool wine and oil, for a third of the day, as we have said; then loosen the abscess, wash and treat it, as it should be, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know universally in the treatment of abscesses: now I have told you how one must go before the treatment of abscesses, and see the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	From the neck come small abscesses, and they are caused by lice that live in our clothing, just as the gnat does on a chicken, and there are many variations of them.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some with fat and such where there is moisture as well as pus; and there are others that are hard and stony in texture, and there is no doubt if the artery does not do otherwise.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the body is that you should test with all instruments called "catheters," from which the form comes afterwards, whatever it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, they draw it out from above.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, they burn it without leaving anything behind that contains the moisture, for it returns as soon as one leaves it; then immerse cotton in Egyptian ointment if it is present; otherwise, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; those who remain overnight will be cured.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then begin the cotton again, as before, the second day and the third, until you are sure it does not hurt at night; then treat the wound with ointment appropriately, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess contains pus and fat, cut it according to this form, lengthwise; and pour out your nails, and scrape off all scabs from all parts, and put all your care into pulling out the arrow where he lies; and if an artery makes a sound against you, do what I told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also treat the abscess if it is stone-like, by cutting and curing as I told you.Car il adont que li maux par la cotte ne se puet guariir, s’il est trop grant ou trop longuement tenus; et si le mal te fait tuit a la cotte, et te trais et te guaris la cotte, et il ne veult demourer en sa place; adonc covient que tu remettes la cure d’icelle, et que tu luis donnes li repos de la cotte, si com je t’ai dit.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the pierreous abscess and moisture is lighter, because it contains little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if there is no moisture in any of these abscesses, either in the head or not, and this was the type of abscess that I incised in the head of an old woman; and I found the abscess just like a hard, rough, white stone, and couldn't be crushed; and if anyone had broken it, they would have made a wound just like a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming out of the head, except for those that come out at the head of children and at the roots of the ears, the opening should be as low as possible so that the pus can flow out; and treat them as they should be.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses come in the neck, and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes they come elsewhere in the body, and are large, and are intertwined with each other.Et sont de poc de sang, et de poc de moiste, et fuient li moiste par la voinne que on leur ouit; et si ne le font, il fuient per les poins des chies, ou il sont venuz; et s’il ne fuient pas per li chief, il fuient per les autres poins.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its coat, as the knot and abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many similarities among these scrofulas.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and others that are malicious and do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	So in that one which you see is of good disposition to touch, and is similar in color to the body, and moves from each part and is not arouses the nerves of the neck or the artery or the conduit, and is not profound; so you must cup it from above, and scrape off each part, and are the two lips of the heart bent inward if you need, as we have said in abscesses of the head; and draw it little by little, and be sure that you do not cover the nerve or vein, and neither the spatumile nor the trenchant so that the hand does not slip, and do not look too far forward so that you do not cover what you should not.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you grasp the vein or artery and it does not let you work, then put powdered vitriol in the wound, or some powder that stops bleeding, and constrict the wound; and leave it until the abscess is eased, and the wound softened and begins to fester.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the bleeding is stopped, return to your task, until you have finished it; then seek out with your finger if any small scrofulae remain, and squeeze and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the scrofula, you must not squeeze that scrofula at its root, but ligature it with a strong double thread, and let it drop without harming; then treat the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, and then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut all around the scrofula, then you should bring together the two lips of the wound and stitch them now, since there is no longer any surplus due to the size of the scrofula.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you should proceed to cut off its root and pull it out, then stitch it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofula which hold surplus, pierce where it appears to be dying; and pierce it thus as the one before is said, depending on it, then administer poultices with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is clean, then treat it with ointment smeared on a bandage until it heals.
de squinance	of squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients spoke of the cutting of the throat; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the record of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squint, the flap of the throat, which is called the "epiglottis", should be cut; and one must not make an incision by this, because all the veins and the lung of the patient are affected by the heat of the abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the throat's canal, one must cover the epiglottis to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we want to split the epiglottis, we should split it below three circles or four, a small split through both circles, or according to the amount of the split in the soft palate; and those places which are subject to the section of the epiglottis where there is no cartilage, and the vessels are long from there.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, then he should stretch the skin of the throat all the way to the Adam's apple, then split the skin until he reaches the gland; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then cut the sinus, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the vein of the gland that jumps out through the place that is broken, and by the failure of the voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed that we doubt strangulation, bring together the two lips of the heart wound, and cut all the way to the cartilage without damaging it; then administer remedies that promote scar tissue growth until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim says to do this only until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged dead, and the lack of breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut the epiglottis so that the patient cannot choke, and he will breathe through the wound, and thus be saved from death; and because of this the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease passed, and it passes in 3 or 4 days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and treat it, once it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young maiden take a knife and thrust it into her throat, and cut part of the veins in her neck; and I was called to heal her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found that the blood which had issued from it, and I saw that she had not coughed up any blood or vomited anything except through her throat, and the blood was flowing out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened and sewed up the wound and healed her until she was cured; and the maiden had no more pain in her throat, and returned to her senses afterward; therefore I say that one should not fear cutting into the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This kind of abscess is called a "hernia in the throat," and it is a large abscess the color of a plum, and it occurs frequently in women; and there are two kinds: natural and accidental; the natural kind has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental kind is of two kinds, one of which is similar to a cyst, and the other kind is like an abscess that comes from an artery; and there is doubt about it, and one should not operate with force except on those that are small, and test and examine all along the entrance: if you find it just like a cyst, and it cannot be removed in any way, then cut into it as one would cut into a cyst, and treat it throughout its entire length, if there is nothing inside; and examine thoroughly, and heal it as it should be healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways to approach this, and I will explain all their similarities; now I must describe the key difference between dislocation and issue.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that discharge is a persistent fever and heat until the swelling has passed, and the pus has been expelled; then the fever and heat will subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a dislocation there is no heat or fever or pain; it contains pus, which is its own sac and is according to the color of the body, and begins like a pimple and becomes swollen; and they appear in two ways, either dry or moist, and their colors are as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the ulcer, that you test and examine it first with all the instruments which are called "syringes", according to what its shape will allow in the chapter which follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the method of inquiring into abscesses is to squeeze the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and move your fingers gradually, until you feel that the pus has broken through the skin, then according to the size of the abscess; then extract the probe, and be careful not to push anything back in.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the pus that flows is clear, whatever color it has, then treat it as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the probe no pus comes out, know that it is fatty, so treat it in a cross pattern, and take it with tweezers, and lightly scrape the skin around where it lies, drawing the pus out with the abscess; and if you cannot draw it all out at once, then treat it bit by bit so that nothing remains.Et se li sembles que li nout est gras et ne peut estre tiriez sain, si fent en la meseure de l’apostoime selonc son grandor; et li sens de li nouts est que s’il a grant dolor sur le corps ou il gist, si est gras, et s’il ne le veult demourer en un leu, si vait ains qu’il ne peut demourer en un leu, et se il adonc le gardait il morut; et ne se doit demourer lons temps, car li est grant danger.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it stays, it will return to us many times; and if it remains for a little while, and the pain is not severe, apply some corrosive powders to the wound, bind it tightly, and put hot poultices on the abscess, treating the wound with other remedies until it heals; and if the nose is large, cut the two lips of the wound, and treat it with a remedy that encourages flesh growth.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein beneath is contrary to you or another, hasten and apply powdered vitriol, and let it remain for 2 or 3 days, until the wound suppurates and the blood flow ceases; then return to cover what has remained uncovered during this time.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See the forms of the trocar, which come in three varieties: large, medium, and small; and there are three types of these, called 'albaret', one called 'breb', and they also come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, to pierce abscesses; and they are like needles used to pierce sorcerers' marks, made from brass, iron, or silver, but the yellow ones are best, and are most often used with black pitch to pierce fistula. They come in three sizes depending on the width of the opening.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of warts are very varied, as you can see: large, medium, and small; and there are warts that have two curves in three ways; and there are warts with three curves, and they are also in three ways; and there are warts with two curves, and warts with only one curve, and they are in three ways; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these knives are sharp, and some only cut one side, so that the nerve or vein is not cut; and there are three types of such instruments: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and they are only used on fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and fingers, and similar places; and sometimes a small instrument like a punch is made according to this form, with which blood is stopped.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and sometimes it is put into the place that heals by copious bleeding of veins and arteries; and sometimes they heal according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Sometimes the breasts of some men swell when they become corrupt, resembling women's breasts; and they remain ugly and swollen, and those who want to cure them should follow this line from b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Scrape off the fat, and treat the wound with ointment, then sew up the two lips of the wound and heal it until it is clean; and if the breast sags and becomes soft due to its size, as happens to women, then make two slits on top, in the form of two similar incisions; so that one lip of the wound is sewn to the other at the end of each slit, ensuring that the larger line contains the smaller according to this shape, from line b to g; then scrape off the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we have said about sewing and powders, and whatever else is necessary for healing, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely done, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then you should fill the wound with damp cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it sucks up the remaining fluid and fat, then heal it until it is clean.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpits
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses which come from under the armpits are like hard scrofula nodules, and some contain pus.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line .b. to line .g.:
