et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And the way to treat it is to instruct the patient to pull the intestine back into the wound with his hand if he can; then hold the scrotum between your hands and lift the testicles; then the anus will be on top, and grab all the skin of the testicles from the long side; then insert the knife tips into the groove of the incision according to what you need in order to open the wound, so that the blood can flow out; then scrape the scrotum under the skin of the testicles until the white tough scrotum is exposed on all sides; then put your index finger into the one that follows the testicle, between the white scrotum which is under the skin of the testicle and between the second scrotum, and separate what is behind the testicle and between the second scrotum; and move your right hand into the scrotum, and hold the white scrotum in your left hand, lifting the testicle up towards the anus; then have the assistant lift the testicle up, and loosen what is under the ligature at the back; and feel with your fingers if there is any intestine wrapped in the tough white scrotum, and if you find anything, put it back into the abdomen; then take a needle with a thick thread made of 10 threads, and insert it into the back part of the scrotum, which is after the skin of the testicles; after the incision, then grab the heads of the threads, so that there are 4 threads; then tie them together one on top of the other in the shape of a cross, and tie the scrotum with a strong ligature in two parts, so that none of the blood vessels that nourish it can enter, otherwise an abscess will form there; then put the ligature back according to the first long ligature, 2 fingers from that one, and after these two leave the scrotum which is under the skin of the testicles with a large portion of the ligature; and after all this, grab the part which is under the skin of the testicles, so that the blood flows, as we have said before; then apply soft wool soaked in oil to the wounds, and apply the ligature which we have described.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And sometimes the white syphilis that we have described is cauterized after the incision, out of fear of bloodletting.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this happens many times, and leave the ligature in place until it cuts through; and if it is slow to fall off, then use a hot water fomentation, and apply what we have said above, until it cuts through; then heal the wound with another healing method, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a fleshy hernia
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this branch, I have never seen anyone dare to perform the cure with iron.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancients said that it is made like the thread which is twisted together with the vis, in such a way that you tie the vessels, after cutting them slightly above and below; then cut them in the middle, and treat the abscess with what we have described, until the vessels are cut through; then heal it as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Sometimes the anus is torn apart, as we have said, and it opens up; but no intestines slip out, and if any do, they quickly go back in; and even if he stays in that position for too long, a fistula forms where the intestines are torn, as we have said, because they are stretched and then become soft and swollen; and this is treated with cautery, as we have said before; and sometimes it is treated by cutting into the anus in the following manner: the patient lies on his back between your knees, and you cut around the edge of the fistula according to its size, about three finger widths wide; then you pull out the fistula which is under the skin, and you press down on the abdomen, and then you cut the two visible openings of the fistula on the anus, and cut them both; then you pull out the head of the fistula, and do not cover up the opening or stretch it open with anything, as I have told you before in the treatment for tears in the intestines; then heal it using the healing method for wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the threads, clean and treat the wound until it heals.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	Syrup is constricting and has no appearance in a hernia, and cauterization is beneficial in this case, and closer to healing.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the skin of the scrotum
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the testicles becomes soft in some men, because the parts within are softened, and it appears milky white; and when one wishes to treat it, he should have the patient lie on his back, and cut away the skin which is softened above the natural skin; then bring together the two lips with a single stitch, and if you see fit, sew the superfluous soft skin with three or four stitches firmly; then cut between the stitches, and treat it as other wounds until it is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	of castration
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	You should know that castration is forbidden in our law, and for this reason I would prefer not to discuss it in this book. It is only necessary for two reasons: the first is so that doctors can answer questions about it and know how to perform the procedure; the second is because we often need to castrate certain animals to help us, such as bulls, rams, and pigs and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castration is performed in two ways: by pulling or by cutting.Li chastremens por atraction est quanque li mires tire le membr’adessus la lande et qu’il le frotte sus li testiculi, si que il se descende; et tant com il le descende, il le tret adissous la lande et adessous les testiculi, et li mires le tret sus la lande et adessus les testiculi; et tant com il tire et frotte, li membr’adessus la lande se desce.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In the one we do by traction, let us sit the animal in warm water until its joints are softened and relaxed; then squeeze them with your hand until they are reset and you feel no more pain.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Of castration of the testicles: you should dye the animal and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand, then tie the scrotum, and cup each testicle with your hand as you squeeze it, once you have squeezed them well; and leave some fat of the testicles and the fine fat that is under the vessels; and this type of castration is better than that which is done by traction, because in traction something from the testicles may remain, causing the animal to desire lust; then cure the wound until it heals.
des hermofrodites	of hermaphrodites
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism occurs in two ways in men: one is that between the two testicles there appears something like the form of nature of a woman, having hair, and sometimes it urinated through it.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other manner is in women, and has over the finger as a wand and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment of men and women is also to cut off the foreskin all around, and treat it as any other wound; in the second manner, for men whose urine drips from the skin of the testicles, there is no treatment.
de la tentigene	of the testicles
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A 'tentigen' is an aberration on the skin, so disfigured that it is horrible to look at; some women have them as large as a hand, and this is the treatment for them.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should dye the excess of the tentigen on your hand or with tweezers, and gently pluck it; do not go too deep so that there is no bleeding, then treat it with another treatment until it is healed; also for a growth that occurs in the mouth, use cow's milk, and perhaps it will disappear, and it is similar in appearance to a mole, and because of this they called it the 'cow disease'.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you need to treat it, as we have said about the tendon, and heal it until it is cured.
de erratique	of Errata
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	If it is errant, when the nature of the woman is not understood, or the opening is small; and it is natural from birth, or an accident from illness that came to it; or it is from a wound made by a sharp object or a thick one, and it is made deep in the belly, or on the sides, or underneath, or wherever; and they should understand conception and childbirth, and by chance the flowers to come; and the knowledge of this is through observing the dance.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the sores are nearly healed, then you can use your fingers or a stick.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is from a sharp object and it is close to the lips, then you should do this: place your two index fingers together, and have the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then form the lips, so that the sharp object can be pushed out, and cover the sores; then take wool, soak it in oil, and place it on the wound, and have the woman lie at home every day so that it may not close up.Si est dou syfac espés, et li estoupemens est prochiens, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the ulcer is hard and thick, then you must cut it with a spatulum resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the discharge is bloody, then dry it and cut it; and have blood-stopping medicines like acacia, dragon's blood, incense, and egg white; then apply a broad piece of pitch so that the wound does not heal; and let it be for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when there is a bloody discharge in the eye, it must be cut in this way, unless it is an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For in the abscess that is in the eye, one should not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	of Hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are openings of veins that discharge blood without usual cause, and when hemorrhoids are old they become thorny; and we have already said in the division their appearances, signs, and I will say here those that receive cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thistles, when they are deep in the anus and do not appear to the touch, are not cured by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the mouth of the anus, one can feel, they are those that one can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you should put the woman in a cold room, then burn the hemorrhoids with tweezers and pull out the roots, then powder it with medicines that stop bleeding, such as myrrh and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then bandage her feet to the wall for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if there is any bleeding, she should sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate bark and gallnuts and similar things, and then take barley flour, boil it with honey and garlic, and use it as a poultice on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it is stopped, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, make him breathe in bellows on the back and on the breasts without piercing; then take linen, soak it in plantain juice or dogwood juice with old wine, and apply it to the affected area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has drained, treat the wound with ointment until it heals; and that which is called "albathir" is red and looks like rough leather, so cover it as I have said before; then treat it until it heals.Et se il estainche, c’est boin.
des apostemes de la marris	Here is the translation of the next sentence:
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	There are many types of abscess that come from the sea, such as ulcers, pustules, herpes, eschar, and hemorrhoids, as well as hot abscesses, and several other diseases which I have mentioned in the division.Et se il estainche, c’est boin.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I describe in this treatise the hot abscess which occurs in the mare, which is not among the abscesses that collect in the bowels; and if you wish to know how it is treated with iron, observe whether the abscess is hard at the beginning of its appearance, and full of heat and fever, and whether it turns red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	So do not be hasty in piercing, but let it bleed until the pain is relieved; and then have the patient sit on a chair, with two small chairs to lean on, and support his back and rest his feet against the ends of his legs; and let his buttocks be spread apart, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a cord; then suck the bag towards the right side, and administer the instrument through which the mouth of the mare is opened, from which the form [of the instrument] comes; and it is necessary that when you see this instrument administered, you insert the rod first to know the depth of the wound so that what goes into the instrument does not go deeper than it should and hurt the patient; and if the instrument is larger, cover the depth of the wound with cloth so that the instrument does not cause pain; and it is necessary that he place the funnel of the instrument on top and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscesses open and they are made on the soft hand, then it is necessary to cover the head with a bandage; and when the bowels are evacuated, then you must put in the wound moist tents in rose oil, or in dry green oil; and put the tent out of the wound at the bottom of the injury, and put a poultice over the injury and over the clean linen wound with moist malva flowers or cooked aristolochia leaves; then cure it after two days of ointment, until it is healed; and sometimes raise the injury and the wound by a clyster of water and honey, and then with water or cooked lilies and aristolochia leaves; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is returned to the injury, then you must guard against cooking with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	It is important for the midwife to first understand the natural process of childbirth and its signs: when you see the woman pushing downward and desiring to smell aromatics, then the child hastens to come out; thus you know that this childbirth follows the natural course, and the placenta comes out with the child, and the mother's excess fluids are expelled through good cleansing. But if it comes in any other way, then it is not natural.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For sometimes the child comes out feet-first, or head-first, or by the arms or from the chest or abdomen; it may also emerge from the side or be turned upside down in some other bad position. Thus the midwife must be wise and cunning in such matters, and beware of errors and deceptions, and I shall show you all the positions and how to assist them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If the child comes out on its head by natural delivery, and the woman gives birth painfully, and her strength is weak, then make her sit on a chair or have women hold her; and give the midwife a small sponge soaked in rose oil or fried fenugreek between her fingers, and then insert it into the child's mouth:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And cut the amnion, and press her nail until the moisture that is within flows out; and press the belly of the woman so that the child comes down, and if it does not come down, then one should cleanse the woman with a poultice of fenugreek with oil of asses' milk; then make her press and sneeze with incense, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: then the child will now come out.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if both hands come out, then you should gently reset them little by little; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a chair, and lift her feet upward; then stand the chair on the ground, and press on the woman so that she does not strain while standing up; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child is dead, then grip the hands with the knife that was mentioned earlier, and extract the child, and reset them in the same way.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	of the issue of the child upon his feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out onto his feet, he should be pushed upwards; and then he is turned slowly, until he is straight; then grab him by the feet and extend him slowly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	When he jumps up to his hips, instruct him to grab hold, and make him sneeze forcefully; if he jumps out, God willing.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not jump out as we have said, then pull it back little by little, until it is in its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For then it will be easy.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if he does not come out as we have described, take the mallow plant and boil it in oil of sesame seed, and crush the gum into it; and put this ointment onto the woman's nature inside, then make her sit in warm water up to her ribs; and when she is softened beneath, place a bandage of myrrh on her, and leave it there for an hour; then make her sit on a chair, then make her sneeze and constrict her mouth and nose, and gently press her belly, for the child will come out now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	for the child to come out onto his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this way, then put your hand gently on his head; then lie him on his back and let his legs hang down, and let him lie on his side; and fold his hands gently, and then press his hands on his belly, and lift up the cushions underneath, so that he is lying on his side; and if the child does not cry out, then take his feet and move them gently, then move his belly upwards, then put your hand in; and rock the child gently; and command the woman to hold on until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	of the child's exit, which comes out wide a hand's breadth
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	I will describe how to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, then have the woman stand up and walk around; if she cannot walk, then make her lie on the bed and raise her legs gently; then administer the musk-moss that I described; and if she does not give birth, then have her sit on a chair, then try to bring back the hand; and rock the child according to nature, and make her sneeze, and command her to hold on until the child emerges.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	from the emerging of the child onto its neck, and spread out his hands, and turn his face towards his mother's back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	It is necessary for the surgeon to dye his hand, then turn it slowly and gently; and when it is even, he should apply a poultice of mustard and oil, as we have said, then instruct her to move it slowly; and when you have done this, make her sit on a chair, and instruct her to grip something; and make her sneeze.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	in the same way for all of the secondine
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes out in this way all over the body, then scrape away the scabs with your fingernail until the moisture is exhausted; and if the infant hangs on her face and neck, scrape him off, so that he is not retained and dies; then put the child back inside, so that you have placed him as he should be, and instruct the woman to grip something a few times: then let go gently.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	Know that twins are born many times, and sometimes triplets or quadruplets; and this is not a strange thing, but happens rarely.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	They are strange things and do not live if they are not named. I know that they are multiplied and separated by the syrup that divides them, which is bound to the jar. Sometimes they emerge as naturally as a tail, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	And if they emerge quickly, the treatment as we have said, and the doctor skilled, and do quickly and skillfully what she does, and act according to how it benefits health.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Sometimes they are formed in the sea one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to fifteen, and all of them are shaped like children according to the measurement of the glorious sage, and it is necessary for the doctor to know this because sometimes similar things happen; then act according to what is appropriate.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you treat a woman for a dead child or womb, as I have said in the division, and there is no movement, and you are forced to use your hands, it is necessary that you know whether the woman has good health and is not afraid of death; then the woman should lie on her back with her head inclined downward and her legs raised. The doctor should apply the ointment to both parts as she performs the massage, either lying in bed so that she is not moved while delivering the child, or on a table if it is easier to deliver the child. Then, rub the mouth of the sea with moist oils infused with myrrh and fenugreek and flax seed; then, the doctor should anoint their hands with these oils and apply the myrrh, then insert the fingers gently into the sea, then massage the place where it is expected to emerge, and watch if the child appears ready to slide down onto the head; then insert the fingers into the eyes, nose, mouth, throat, or armpits, and if delivery is from the feet, insert them at the heels and under the knees. It is necessary to anoint the right hand with the ointment and place the palm between their left thumb and forefinger, then gently massage the whole hand, and insert a finger in any of the places we have mentioned, as long as it comes to the empty space; and this is the shape of the finger:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	then pierce against the other nail, or the third if you need it, so that the extractions are even; and then they are made even by moving from one side to the other, so that they may move out, and let the nails bite to hold them in place, as the form is:
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part remains, then anoint the ball with oil, and push it into that part, and pull out the other; and if nothing remains, put this nail in a higher place, and do this until everything comes out.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be pulled due to tightness, then you must wrap it with a cloth until it goes out; then the joint in the palm or at the wrist, and thus you should do for the other hand, and also for the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the child is large and it is narrow in the outlet, and it has a sharp pain gathered at its head, then you must insert the spathumile between your fingers, piercing the head and extracting the fluid; or you can pierce it with the instrument called "almidach", from which the form comes with the instruments or chapter that follows this one; and likewise, do the same if the infant has a large natural head; and then pull out the bones with tongs, and if the head pops out and is pulled forcefully, it will be split open so that the moisture that is in the outlet can escape; and if it cannot come out, then cut it into pieces as much as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then you must pierce it so that the moisture flows out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on his feet, the pulsing is light, and the pulse at the mouth of the wound is weak.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is stricken in the belly or the foot, then you should draw it out by the cloth wrapped around the hand; and make an incision in the belly or the foot, until the moisture that is there runs out; and if the other members are drawn out, and the bowels remain, then he puts his hand into the wound up to the depth of the wound; then he puts in one or two fingers, and draws it out; and if the mouth of the wound is narrowed by a hot abscess that has come there, then one should not work on it, but rather apply moist and fatty things; and the provider applies poultices, and uses warm and softening water.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the fetus is on his side, and you can make it even, then one should administer what we have said for a living child; and if one cannot, then he draws it out in pieces, and leaves nothing of the placenta.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if pus is present in the wound, as happens in maritime wounds, and there is bleeding, it should be stopped with a constrictive bandage, and other treatments administered.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose fetus had been dead inside her belly; then another was sewn over it, and the other one died as well.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, an abscess came in her armpit, and it swollen so much that it opened up and began to discharge profusely.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought long and hard, but could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong attracting poultice, and out came a bone, and after a few days, some more.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very astonished, because the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that they were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I probed the wound and extracted some bones until the woman was in a better state; she lived for a long time like this, but sometimes there would be a little discharge from the site. I have included this chapter mainly because when a master encounters something unusual, he should know how to provide relief.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the dislocation back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the press, with which one is equipped in books; and at two turns of the two sides of the two lines.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Nevertheless, the probe should be more subtle than the constrictive bandage and made of ebony or boxwood; the mouth of the tool should be two fingers wide, and its edges smooth, and about a palm and a half long; and in both sides there should be two adjustments of this same wood, which are firmly fixed on either side, about a palm or a little more in length; and these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the wound to open it when one turns the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, with a more subtle and lighter appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the appearance of tongs; and has two adjustments at its ends, as you can see, one palm long, and two fingers wide; and when you see to open the wound all over the instrument, then let the woman lie on the bed, her feet hanging down and her legs open, then fit the two adjustments together in the wound, and hold the head of the instrument between her thighs; then work your hand over the instrument, just as you did with the tongs, according to the amount that you see opening the mouth of the wound, until the midwife does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all tapered and have multiplied their likenesses; and when the operator has prepared them, they are more nimble in their work and more effective for people due to their quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not despair of the instrument until you have prepared it, for their necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the placenta is retained during childbirth, then you must instruct the patient to hold in her breath, and then make her sneeze with some scent, and hold your hands over her mouth and nose; and if she breathes out through that, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, one should take a pot and make a hole in the lid, and place herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as calendula, rue, anise, chamomile, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water over fire; then put one end of the pot into the hole, and the other end into the mouth of the wound, and hold it there until the vapors enter the wound; then make the patient sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then the scabs will fall off quickly.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and is not cured, one should command the midwife to moisten her left hand with oil of sesamum or with a poultice of aloe, and then insert it into the birth canal, and feel for the placenta; and when she finds it, she should grasp it and gently extend it straight, so that the wound does not tear during extraction; but she must move it slightly to the right and left, and then pull; it will come out and separate.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the ulcer is open, we have spoken of the cure of sneezing and of the fumigation of herbs; and if it is not cured by all that we have said, then beware that you do not play with fire; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the ulcer, that you tie it to the thigh of the woman, then cleanse her with an ointment of tetrafarmacon; she will vomit and be relieved, but nevertheless, when she vomits, a foul odor comes to the stomach and the head, and the disease becomes worse.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If this is the case, then suitable smoke treatments are needed: some of the ancients have tried smoke from watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument with which one smokes out the woman is for the retention of flowers and secondine if it is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like glass in appearance, and one puts the fine end into the nature, and the wide ends above the fire; and there is fumigation over the coals, and the stain until it is wasted away, and then another one begins.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the anus pierced, but instead have a small subtle fissure; therefore it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that fissure with her finger, and not to pierce it with a sharp instrument, and to guard against breaking the membrane; then she should put moist linen in wine and oil on it, then cure it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will heal, put a wooden peg in the hole and leave it for several days, then remove it when the child wants to go to bed.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes the clotting comes suddenly from a wound or abscess; then it must be covered suddenly: then it should be treated, as we have said, with a peg of wood.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula in the anus
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the anus are nodules, and they grow larger than those that come from within the anus, or in the space between its two parts, whether there is one fistula or several. And when this nodule becomes old, it opens up, and usually white pus or thin fluid leaks out, and sometimes these fistulas burst; and they are apparent when there is either urination or flatulence, or both, when the patient urinates, and sometimes a burst occurs.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that pierce all the way to the bladder, and halfway down the shaft of the penis; and they can reach the hip joint, and the head of the thighbone.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows a bursting fistula in the anus, and not a non-bursting one: and it is when you push your finger into the anus, and insert a thin needle made of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no twisting.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is twisting, then insert a thin tent made of lead, or a horse hair, as far as you can feel the tent or the hair with your finger; and if you cannot feel it, and no urination, flatulence, or pus comes out, as we have said, then you know that it has not pierced through; so be quick about treating it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has reached the bladder or the urinary tract, and the urine flows out, and it cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perceived just to the joint of the thigh, then the vein is flowing just to the spot; if there is no twisting and the pain is felt all around, then it is that it has become swollen immediately, and neither medicine nor poultice is of use; and in these persisting fistulas there is no cure other than effort, and futility of the foolish meddling of those who interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that which is not persisting and is not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient lies on his back, and the doctor lifts his legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs inclined towards his belly; then insert a tent of bronze, or of lead if there is twisting, as far as you know where the vein flows.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the anus, then you must insert your index finger there, if without feeling that the tent has pierced it; and it should be uncovered where you feel the swelling or lump, then you know that it is persisting; then work on it no more for one cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can indeed heal some of them, but this happens rarely; and the help one provides is to heat the cautery subtly according to the width of the fistula, as has been said before; and insert it into the fistula all the way to the bottom, doing this two or three times until you know that the false membranes have been burned, which look like a feather; then cleanse with moist tenters, until those membranes come out, then treat with ointment to heal and seal.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is thus healed, it is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is thus healed, all is well; but if the tent is inserted and does not pierce to the root which is at the bottom, and there is between your finger and the tent a thick covering of false membrane or pus, and you see the fistula above this covering of the flesh; then cut away from the beginning of the fistula, and insert the cautery again before the tent, going down to the chief of the tent; and the tent will be released and fall out; then scrape off those false membranes which look like a feather, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pus flows out, and enters between you and the wound, then cauterize it with fire or a medicinal agent.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	Because fire cautery brings together two things: the scorching of the flesh and the stemming of blood and drying of moisture; then treat the tent with butter or crushed substance, until the wound weeps, and the charred flesh comes out with the weeping; then treat the wound with a poultice of dry medicaments.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way from the fundament, and is separated from the body, put your finger in it or in the fundament, and explore inside.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you sense the tent and within it is thread or char, or it is about to pierce, then there must be a way of hope and expectation through one of three means: either cauterize as we have said, or cut all the way to the bottom; if you can, insert tents and treat as before; be careful not to go too deep, lest you cut the tissue that holds the foundation, and let the discharge flow freely from there; then treat it as we have said; perhaps it will heal. Or remove that covering and cleanse after it is cut away from the foundation, by tent or other pointed instrument; then cauterize the charred flesh in the wound, as much as you can; then aim to restore the wound and keep the fistula in the part away from the foundation: this way the patient will feel less pain.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes the fistula occurs in this way: and it is when you place the tent in the fistula, and it is on the side of the foundation below the skin above, so take a tent pierced at the top according to this shape.
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he puts a twisted thread into 2, and puts the tent all the way through the thread into the fistula as far as the tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it pierces through the margin of the foundation inside, then pull out the thread from that hole so that you can place your finger on the foundation; and pull on the thread's end, and bring the two heads together, and press them tightly against each other, and leave it for a day or two; and sometimes they must be pressed, until the threads cut through the flesh that is between them, then cure the wound until it is healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not open, then make it open in every way you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For one must not bandage it tightly for a long time, and then treat the wound as we have said, until it is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the spatulous bone used to make the fistula is sharp on one side, and smooth on the other; because it should not pierce where it should not, as you can see in the figure.
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two types: they can be inside the anus, like grains of resin, and there can be small or large ones, and some discharge blood, and there can be one or more of them, and they can protrude from the anus and the area around it; but those that protrude have less moisture, and may still discharge a little blood or a little yellow water, and they are colored like the rest of the body. The treatment for those inside the anus is to instruct the patient to straining to go to the bathroom until the hemorrhoids come out, and then you can see the veins; so you hurry and grab them with tweezers or your fingernail, and then cut them at their roots; and if the nails cannot hold them due to moisture, they are grabbed with a cloth, or cotton, or a piece of camel's hair; and then pull them out with your fingers, and then cut them, and powder some hot powdered cautery on top of them; or you can cauterize them as described in the chapter on cautery, and then treat other hemorrhoids until they are healed; and if the anus cannot come out, then the patient is given a strong and harsh enema to clean what is inside the anus so that it can come out clearly; when the patient strains, and if the hemorrhoids have come out of the anus, then the treatment is simple; you grab them with your fingernail or tweezers, and cut them, and then treat them as we have said until they are healed and fear incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should administer the stitch in the following manner: take a twisted thread and insert it into a needle; then pull the thread through from the top and pierce the needle through from the other side, and turn both ends of the thread beneath the needle, making sure it is tight; then tie off the thread, remove the needle, and do likewise with all the others, leaving one to draw out any excess blood; then place a damp cloth moistened with rose oil or cerate over the wound, and command the patient to rest; and then let him remain until he passes stool, and when it has passed, treat it with ointment and other remedies until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from dryness of the penis or anus
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is dryness of the bowels due to constipation, and because of the natural confinement, and when the illness is old and medicine does not help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	You should cut away at the edge of a wound with a spatulum or your fingernail, ensuring that it is not moist; then treat it until it scabs over as it should; and if it cannot scab, then repeat the scraping more aggressively than before, until it heals well and is scoured; then treat it until it is healed.
dou fremit	where there is trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ants are a small appearance fretted under the body, and very much go through the body; and sometimes the frost bites them, and one feels them like death in trembling, and they come all over the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a candle made of goose fat or fat of a wild bird, and put this candle on the trembling, until the purple circle surrounds the trembling; then turn your hand around the entire candle, until you grip all around the trembling, and push it deep inside, and draw out the trembling from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that it is made of an iron or steel candle according to this form, and it is subtle underneath and drawn above:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so as to hold the wound, and to press it And if you see that the wound is cauterized, as in the chapter on cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes the enema is made of silver or brass, or molten copper or hammered; and sometimes they are made from these small and large instruments, according to those who use them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who administer treatment for children and the feeble and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the enema, whether small or large, is placed above, or the abdomen is bound according to this method:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And there is a bagging where the belly is tied, as you see, and the anus is pierced inside; and it has two openings on one side, and one on the other; and the belly is made into a pouch of a beast's bladder or parchment, and pierced all around with small holes, and there should be one inch between each hole, then insert strong thread twisted in an X or in a spiral around, and assemble the belly as a goat; and when the medicine is inside, attach it to the instrument in front with a strong string, then catheterize; and this is the shape of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	Let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head of the catheter with oil or egg white, or similar, then insert it gently; then the minister squeezes his two hands together, so that it is completely empty, then remove the catheter, and let the patient lie with his legs against a wall, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him strain as much as he can; and if he sleeps all night like this, it is more helpful.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you syringe him for a disorder of descending stomach, and the medicine rushes out, then you repeat it until he is healed.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the anus or an abscess, then let the catheter be as thin as for a child; and this is the shape of the subtle catheter under which the skin is stretched:
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the division the cure of wounds; now we will discuss manual and medicinal cures according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and by what they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by the hitting of stone, and cutting with sword or knife, or lance or staff or arrow, or similar; or that they are made according to the parts of the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or head, or leg, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with simple wounds of the head, for their memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, then take care if it is from a blow of stone or similar things, and the skin is still broken and the wound is large, and you quickly doubt a hot abscess: then make him bleed from the cephalic vein immediately if there is little blood coming from the wound, and let the bleeding be in the opposite direction to the injured part; and let the patient avoid fullness of wine and rich foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bleed, then let his food be diminished, and do not drink wine or eat meat; and put cotton soaked in rose oil only, or in astringent wine on the wound if hot abscesses come from it; and if there is no hot abscess, then put powder on the wound, if it is fresh with all its blood, and has not been moved by air; I will describe this powder a little later. And if it has been moved by the fire, then put some ointments on it until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a sword cut and similar, and the lips cannot be closed with sutures, then close it by sewing it shut, as I will describe for abdominal wounds.
