Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and can be peeled back, and is only attached by a small piece of skin, then cut it away; next, cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse foods such as testes and cooked wheat, as well as meat, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find pus in the skin, and it is not attached to the bone, then cut away the pus, and if there is a vein or artery in the wound causing blood to flow, and it cannot be staunched with medicine, then tie off the artery, and if that does not help, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the treatment is easy: you should put this powder on so that the burn has healed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of making the powder is as follows: take incense one part, dragon's blood two parts, and quicklime three parts, and grind it into a fine powder, and apply it to the wound, and bind it tightly so that it is well absorbed and joins with all its blood; then dress it well, and leave it uncovered if there is no swelling; for one does not remove the medicine until it has healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one applies chalk alone when one does not have incense or dragon's blood, but one should move the wound with the cautery.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound has been moved by the fire, let it be in the same state, and do not apply any of this powder to it; but apply some digestive ointments, or barley flour made with water and honey, until it heals; then cure it with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	If the fracture of a bone comes with the wound, and it is small, I will extract it with delicate pincers; and I will tell you about fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound on the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is single, there is no difference between it and that of the head, except that the nerves or artery of the neck are cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a nerve, there is nothing else to do but let the cure proceed, and not apply anything constricting, for it hurts the nerves and makes them withdraw; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest member; but use warm medicines, such as hot water washed in cool water, and cooked in honey with rosemary oil, and also washed in cool water, and other minor stones according to this manner, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then cut it and bind it, then heal it until it is cured.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is chapped and full of pus, then pierce it or a lower place; and if an artery is cut, and bleeding ensues, then stop it, and cauterize it if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the windpipe, and the passage for food is blocked, then cut the windpipe on the side of the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape; and then bind it firmly, and leave it for a few days, then treat it with poultices until it heals; and if the wound has left an impression in the bone, then probe it; and if there are pieces of bone, then remove all that you can, and leave those that you cannot reach until the wound heals and the wound is cleaned and the passage cleared. And if the wound is fresh, then apply powder to the powder as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I said in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a blow from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then examine whether the wound bleeds profusely: then you will know that the wound is mortal; and if it is not deep, and it is fresh with all its blood, then do not put the powder on in the first hour, nor ligature it because of the bleeding that occurs profusely and returns to the heart, and heals the patient; but apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you have no ointment, then put old cotton in the wound to draw out moisture, and let the patient sleep on the wound for three days, or four, or more; then no spasms, nor bad tremors of the heart, nor strangulations of the bowels will come; and when you see good signs, then you will know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Heal it then with poultices and other remedies until it is healed; and if it cannot heal and the wound persists, you will know that there is a fistula; treat it accordingly.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a sword or knife, and it is simple, in the front or back, treat it as described above; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, treat it with powder, and if it is deep in the bone, and pieces have come out, clean the wound, and draw out the foreign objects if they are not stuck; and if they are stuck, let the wound fester to loosen the objects, and then extract them; and for other wounds on other parts of the body, the treatment is as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	of a rupture of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	There are great, medium, and small ruptures of the belly; from the large rupture sometimes the intestines, or the nerves of the intestines, protrude through the wound; and stitching is more difficult, and sometimes a small rupture is worse than a large one because it is harder to stitch up the intestines gradually, placing them back in little by little as they are heated, for the intestines swell immediately when they feel cold, so they are placed back in more easily, and for this reason a small wound is better, as one can gradually return the intestines to their place. And know that there are four types of rupture of the belly: the two common ruptures occur in belly stitching, and the ruptures of other wounds on the body; and the other two types are specific to belly ruptures, and I will describe each type and explain them.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and something from the intestines protrudes out, and it is difficult to put back in, it is due to one of two reasons: either because of the size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in such a way: moisten a sponge or soft cloth in lukewarm water, or cook it in squinch-water with cyprus and spice, and rub the intestines until the swelling goes down; sometimes this wine binding remedy helps to reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling subsiding, wet or warm the intestines with water in which alder and mallows have been cooked, because it is harmful to cut into it without great necessity; and if it cannot be inserted, make a small incision in the wound using an instrument used for hemorrhoids; and the first remedy is better than cutting, which should not be done without great necessity; and the instrument for splitting it: insert it into the wound and push it out, and observe the shape:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines pop out, he must be put back together according to his natural shape in his own place, if you have the power, for this is better.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is low in the abdomen, you should make the patient lie on his back with his legs raised higher than his head. If it's high in the abdomen, then he should lie on his side with his head and feet higher than his torso. If the rupture is in one of the sides of the abdomen, then he should be positioned so that the injured part is higher than the other. You should arrange things as I instruct for both large and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what you have available and hold in your hand a pair of forceps that covers the entire wound edge, then bring the two edges together; this is the common method of stitching, which is to pierce both sides of the skin and the underlying tissue with an needle, through all four edges simultaneously. Then, pull the needle through with a double thread, tie off the ends, and repeat as needed according to how many stitches are required for the wound. The needles should be medium-sized, neither too fine nor too thick, so that they can pierce the skin and underlying tissue without further damaging the wound. After stitching, pad the needle heads or ties with cloth to prevent discomfort when lying down. Leave the stitches in place until the wound is healed. This method of stitching with needles is best for smaller wounds, as it requires fewer stitches. The second common method is to bring together just the skin and underlying tissue edges with a single needle and thread; once all four edges are pierced, pull the needle back through the starting point, in the manner of sewing cloth. Leave about half an inch between each stitch. This method worked on a man with a large abdominal wound that had been made by a knife, with intestines protruding two inches from the wound.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned the intestine after it had been outside for 24 hours, and the wound was sewn shut for 15 days, and I treated it, and it healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they had judged that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where one could not find any medicine; and I put clean cotton on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until it healed.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you about two proper methods of suturing: take the needle and thread it through from one side to the other; when it has pierced right through from one side to the other, then tie off the thread where you threaded it on the needle, and make it pierce through again from the other side to the first; and the idea behind this type of suturing is that you sew just like a tailor sews pelts, and you leave some space between the stitches on one side, and pull tight on the other, until the wound is completely closed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galen describes properly, is like how one joins two pieces of wood naturally and applies the end of one to the other, in such a way: pierce an needle through the tip of the foreskin close to the glans, and only pierce that spot, leaving the two ends of the foreskin; then turn the needle and pierce from the outside in until you reach the inside, piercing through both ends of the foreskin; then pierce one and then the other from the outside in until you reach the inside, in two other tips of the foreskin that are on the other side; and this is the most common and best method of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this, and some testify to it, that one should stitch the abdomen with two needles, with thread in each; and one must push one needle from one side and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds; and know that when the rut is on the belly, the stitching is more painful than in other places on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are such as the judgments of other wounds: and it is when you find the fresh wound full of blood, so that the burn has moved, then put back the intestines, and the coat; then put on the powder charm, and if the burn has moved, then put on some ointment that is present, until the wound heals; then cut the threads, and sew the stitches, and the mirach; then cure the wound as the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicine, then put on, as soon as it begins to heal, old cotton, and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	Because you don't need any other medicine for many dispositions where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will cause community to the principal members, then it is necessary to moisten a light pad in tempered heat oil, or rose oil, and place it around the anus, and under the buttocks; and if there is pain or porridge in the bowels, and it happens many times, then enema with warm black wine, and likewise if the porridge comes just to the intestines; and pierce it inside, and know that when it's the large intestines, it is easier to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine which is called "young" cannot heal when it is raw, and this is due to the thinness of the veins through which it is, and the subtlety of the whole body, and its proximity in nature to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the vein leaps out of the wound, then put it back as well as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, then you should tie up the area that is black so that bleeding does not occur there, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut off what is between the ligature, and hang the two ends down from the part below the wound to ease extraction when the vein breaks, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the wound from the boiling
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is pierced, and the wound is small, then one can restore it in some men, for I saw that a man was wounded in the belly with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became a fistula, and the excrement and flatus escaped through it; I applied treatment according to what I could, and did not cease to suturing until it healed, and the edges were sewn together.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewn up, I doubted that the patient had an illness in his belly; but he had no ill, but remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it must be bound in such a way: take a large thread, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened its mouth, place it on top of the two lips, so that it stretches his mouth shut; and then tie the head of the thread, and it will stay so that he cannot untie it, then put another thread after in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed; and then cut the thread.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If these threads enter the intestine and do not harm the patient, one can sew up the intestine with a fine thread cut from the intestine of an animal, in such a way: take the end of this intestinal thread that is well chewed, then tie to this intestinal thread a fine linen thread, twisted, then put the thread through a needle, and sew up the wound, and tie it up in a knot; and this method of sewing with threads is safe only according to the way of hope and expectation; and if the wound is large and wide, especially when it is in one of the grails of the intestines, there is nothing that can be done but subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it wakes up, is universally called a "fistula", and especially when it is swollen and becomes bowed inwards.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the verdant nodule, a hardened and white swelling, where there is no pain, and is bowed in like the beak of a bird; sometimes it is clear and bowed out, and other times thick; sometimes small, and sometimes large; I have already spoken of these in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and has no pus, is caused by one of nine things: namely, through a deficiency of blood or flesh; or due to wickedness; or because there is hard matter within, and on the surface, that does not allow pus to form; or there is too much swelling; or the location is poor, and the matter is of bad quality; or the medicine used is ineffective; or the corruption is of a pestilential nature; or due to the nature of the region where digestion and healing are slow, and swelling occurs naturally; or there are veins or bones involved: I have already demonstrated all these causes, their signs, and medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Then I will tell you about the treatment for a fistula, which is done manually.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You should know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, from the syrinx, or intestine, or bladder, or any of the ribs, or from the spine of the back, or from any joint of the hands or feet; and they can also affect the principal organ of a limb, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this way are a difficult cure, and there is only labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to the place I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it, then take an iron or tent, if the fistula is straight, so pick it; and if the fistula is crooked, then seek with a thin tent of lead, for the lead bends around the bend; and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot pick it well with tents, then cleanse it by enema through one of the openings, for moisture travels from one opening to another, and cleanses; then press it strongly in your hand, so that you know if there is bone or nerve, and feel if it is deep, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press; and when you truly know the location, and whether it is distant from a joint, or nerve, or artery or vein, or any of the places I told you, then treat it according to what I have said, and remove the foreign matter and corrupt flesh within; and then cure it until it is healed; and if the fistula is very deep and straight, then you must probe deeply, as much as you can, then place moist tents in medicine water, and insert them into the chief of the fistula, so that the medicine corrodes the excess that remains at the bottom; and then apply healing ointments to healthy flesh, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize as we have said; and if the bone is damaged by the fistula, then probe it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or nerve bothers your limbs primarily, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is decay and blackness, then treat it as you would a wound until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns to its previous state, know that you have not gone deep enough: probe and dig until you reach the bottom, and remove all the decay, then restore the area; and if it is healed in this way, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the decay is too deep for you to reach it; then there is nothing more to be done except to let nature take its course; and if there is a small corrupt bone, and you can pull it out with tweezers, or with whatever instrument is suitable for this purpose, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, one by one; and if moisture causes a contrary effect, and there is no error or fear, then cut and dry, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in one hour, place something on the wound to promote suppuration, and let it fester around the bone, and then the bones will come loose more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as in the leg or thigh, just clean away the corruption until all the blackness is gone, then dress the wound; and if there is a large amount of rottenness, and it goes right down to the bone marrow, then it must be cleaned out and packed with a poultice right down to the corruption, and then the wound should be treated until it heals. And I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take example and help from your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of about 30 years old who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from inside the body, so that the matter came to the leg and it was swollen with a large abscess, and there was no reason to drain it; but they treated it so foolishly that they caused the abscess to rupture, and a lot of matter flowed out, and it became a fistula, and many holes opened up all over his leg, through which pus and moisture from the body flowed profusely; and many doctors treated him for two years, and there was no one skilled in the art of medicine who could help, so I was called to see him.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of the openings, and then searched all the openings, and found that one led into another all over the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	So I hurried and cut into one of the openings until I exposed a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced, and the corruption extended to the bone inside; I removed what appeared to me of the rotten bone, and thought there was no more corruption except for what I had taken out; and I began to heal the wound with strong medicines for a long time, but could not close it; so I started again, and exposed the bone as before, and found the corruption continued in the bone, so I removed it, and then healed it with medicines; and it was healed and closed quickly, and there was no need to restart the operation except because of the weakness of the patient who could not bear it, and because of the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often the blood-letting bled profusely, but he was completely healed, and a hard lump grew in place of the bone, and he was in good spirits and had no discomfort or pain anywhere, nor when walking or running.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, one should treat it in this way: take a thread, and tie it to the head of the exposed bone, and have someone pull it upward; and take another larger thread of linen, and tie it over the lump that is above the bone, and hold the head steady, so that you draw out the corrupted flesh from below, and expose the flesh where you see the corruption, so that the thread does not cut into the flesh; and place a hot iron or a wooden splint beneath the bone to cover the corrupted flesh; and one must keep pulling until one can see and feel the corruption, and then pull again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is corrupted and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the flesh all around; then put a firebrand underneath, and then bind the corruption from one side to the other, and bind the wound near the site of the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cut the corrupted joint, and bind the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the area between two joints, there is no other way to treat it except by cutting; and if the corruption is at the knuckle of the hand or the foot, then this thing is very difficult, but you must still inquire into the nature of the corrosion, how it presents itself to you; and clean it in every way you can, but be careful not to harm the vein or nerve; and know that there are many methods for binding these bones, depending on the structure of the bones and their appearance, their thickness and thinness, their size and smallness, and their hardness. And therefore, you must prepare an instrument for each type of work; and know that your art will show you the instrument you need, according to your knowledge of this craft, and the testimony of the ways of sickness; so choose the instrument you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The heads may suffer harm due to internal causes or external ones; and when you have treated this corrosion with remedies, yet it does not improve, then one must cover the affected limb up to where the corrosion occurs, so that the patient escapes death, or the greater evil of the defect in the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, as though burnt by fire, and then it turns red after the blackness, then this corrosion spreads from limb to limb, and affects the whole body; so be quick to cover it, and if it is due to the sting of some venomous creature, such as a scorpion, viper, or similar, and the corrosion is on the head, then cover it, and do not give it space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, then cover it at the joint so that the corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, then cover it at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, then it is fatal, and there is no remedy beyond reducing the quantity of the poison; and so also do for the leg: if the corrosion is in the first joint, then cover it after the other joint; and if it is on the foot, then cover all the foot; and if it climbs up the leg, then cover at the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is no remedy except to cut off the limb and let the patient die; and the way to cover the limb with a bandage is that you bind it above and below, and extend one bandage downward from the upper binding, and another bandage upward from the lower binding, and you loosen the flesh between the two bandages by a span wide, so that the bone is exposed; then cover it with a bandage, and place a linen cloth on each side so that the bandage does not touch the healthy part, lest the patient suffer further injury or an abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If bleeding occurs when you operate, cauterize the site thoroughly or apply restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete. Then bind the injured limb with suitable bandages and treat it until it heals. I will tell you what happened to a man who had a dark discoloration resembling a burn on his leg: The corrosion first appeared on his big toe, spreading to his entire foot. When the man saw the corrosion, he wrapped his foot, and it healed. Long after, the corrosion reappeared on his finger, and he came to me. I applied repulsive substances after purifying his body, but I couldn't stop the corrosion. He wanted me to cut off his hand, but I refused, as I had no hope of repelling the matter, and I was afraid that if I amputated his hand, he would die, for his vitality was weak. He despaired completely, returned home, wrapped his hand, and healed. I have only told this story so that others may learn from it and know what to do if they encounter a similar case.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	There are times when an abscess forms in a fleshy part, and remains so long that it creates a great gathering of pus; and then they rupture and drain, and the pus flows out, leaving the place hollow, just like a vessel; and the skin on top is as thin as a piece of cloth, and does not extend to the bone or nerve, and such a disease is called 'sain', and is not called 'fistula'; but if it becomes so prolonged that it reaches the bone in a deep place, then it is called 'fistula'; and the skin is such that you can cover all of this skin all around, and especially when it is thin, just like a piece of cloth; and it does not become infected because of its thinness.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have reason to believe that the skin is becoming infected, and the infection is not deep, and the flesh is thick, then use this enema: examine whether the breast is swollen, and the pus within has a foul odor, then prepare an Egyptian medicine in this way: take ash, and oil, and litharge, in equal amounts, and place it in a vessel over fire, until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take some according to your need, and dissolve it in water and honey, and use it for an enema on the breast, and compress the orifice; and leave the medicine inside for two hours, then remove it by squeezing it out; do this several times, until the breast is cleaned, and the pus is eliminated; and sometimes an enema of water from ashes is used when this medicine is not available, and you take vine ash, and pour water over it, and let it drain, and use it for an enema, until you know that the breast is cleansed; and if the patient cannot tolerate the Egyptian medicine or water from ashes, then use water and honey with a little litharge ground in it; or you may use an emulsion of honey and wine, so that the honey has properties of cleansing and washing, and the wine causes the abscess to drain; and when you have done this, and you have reason to believe that the breast is cleansed, then use an enema of something that makes flesh grow within it, and take a diaphoretic ointment, and mix it with rose oil and wine; or you may use any medicine or ointment of which I have spoken in the section on ointments; and if the orifice of the breast is small, and the tip of the enema cannot enter, then enlarge it with a needle, and place a tent made of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, inside so that it reaches as far as it can go; and if the wound is too large, then cut it and leave only enough space for the enema to enter, and if the orifice that drains pus is above, then cover it, or cover it below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Because when the bowels are at a standstill, you should not allow food to enter; and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, then arrange things so that the bowels move to the lowest place they can, for when the bowels are at a standstill, you should not allow food to enter, and if you cannot cover the breast underneath as you wish, then arrange things so that the bowels move slightly downward, and do not leave anything of the bowels; and take consolidating medicines to put over the wound, and let them be on top of the linen drape that covers the entire wound; then tightly cover the opening of the breast where it is widest above the first, then apply ointment over the other drape according to the amount of the opening, and place it over the opening of the wound to loosen the bowels, and do not remove the large drape for several days; and often remove the one on top of the opening of the breast to loosen the bowels, and test what comes out of the bowels, whether it is venom or pus, or clear, or digested, or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in such a way and you see the nature that appears on top of the wound, then know that the breast is healing, and approach the wound; and then loosen it in the morning, or midday, and when you loosen the wound, change the other drape, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast flows yellow bile after many days, know that the breast does not open.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons spread over a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are those who suffer long-term wounds in their flesh, and of those whose wounds heal the opposite way; and if digested bile rises from the breast after many days, know that the breast is not healed; and if the breast takes a long time to heal and is distant, then apply dry medicines that are moist in substance but dry in nature, such as diaphanous ointment, for it contains a large amount of vitriol, and it is the last medicine; take diaphanous ointment and make it with rose oil, and the rose of old wine which is equal in substance; then cook it and use it; and that same thing is done to thickened honey when diaphanous ointments are not present, or you take myrrh and aloes and incense, and grind them into powder over the honey while it is on the fire; and then glue a cloth over it, and place it over the breast, and sometimes aristologus which is long, and roots of celestial lilies, which is as fine as flour and centaury; and use simples or compounds: grind them into powder, and apply them over the honey that I mentioned earlier, and use them; and if the fistula takes a long time to heal and is not healed by this treatment, then know that the corruption has reached the bone, and causes hard swelling in the bones or limbs, or in the soft tissues; so the cure for the fistula is as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of an abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panaris is an abscess that arises under the nail of the finger or toe, or occasionally elsewhere; and when it becomes infected, and no attention is paid to it, then the abscess grows, and it runs and oozes pus as far as the root of the nail, and sometimes all the way down. And it eats away at the bone, causing a foul-smelling pain, and the area around the nail becomes swollen, and the color turns yellow.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the previous section, and the treatment does not help, then you should trim away all the excess tissue around the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cautery is a great help if the bone and nail are healthy; and if the nail starts to grow over the wound, and it becomes infected, then you should place a piece of hot iron under the nail to scorch the flesh, and push it upwards, and carefully trim away the infected flesh, and apply burning and corrosive medications to remove everything; then treat with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and pull it out, because as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see the toe become corrupted, cut it off at the first joint as previously described, then treat it until it heals; and if it becomes gangrenous and swollen, and causes great pain, then you must treat it first; then cut the nail of the sprain with a diagonal cut, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh under the nail, because the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, place something over it to soothe.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain of a sore tooth in the jaw
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two big toes that grow on the hands of some men by chance are all flesh, and by chance there is bone in it, and sometimes there is a nail; and sometimes they grow at the root of the toe joint, or the growth is in one of our toes.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	He who is born with an extra digit on his hand does not change, but he who is born with an extra digit at the joint of his hand sometimes changes; the size of a person with fleshy digits is slight, in such a way: cut it at its root with a wide spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born in the root of the joint, if he is painful to cure, hold him tightly.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For he who is born with an extra digit on his foot, you should first cut the flesh around it to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable thread, then treat it until it heals.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	Judgments that come to both together come by birth, or by sudden wound, or by burn from fire, or similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Then you should cut the digit so that the fingers grow according to their natural form; then place between two wet tents or drapes moistened in rose oil so that they do not stick together; or place between two pieces of thin wood so that they adhere, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If sudamen comes to any of his hands with the palm, he catches it as appropriate.
des vils	of the villains
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large enveloping vessels full of melancholy excesses, which come in many parts of the body; and they occur more in legs of those who walk on foot and who work and carry loads, than in others.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore you should administer to him sometimes a purgative of collyrium, and then heal it with basil.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment with fire is in two ways: one is to press it and draw out the black blood; the other way is that you open the vein and draw it all out.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	Amputations are done in the following way: first, heat the leg with very hot water until the large veins are dilated, then stretch the leg from above the thigh to the joint below the knee; then cut the vein in one place, or two or three, with a wide incision, then open and draw out the black blood to your hand, from one end to the other, as much blood as the patient can tolerate; then ligate it and command that he eat meats with black pepper; and restart the bleeding and the cauterization when the veins are full, and bandage the wound.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The treatment of the wound is as follows: raise the leg of the patient, if there is much hair, then put it in the bath, and heat the leg with hot water until it turns red and the veins swell; and if you do not have a bath, heat it over the fire, and then cut the skin at the top of the wound, from the knee to the ankle, or in the part below the ankle; then open the skin around the wound, so that it appears when touched; and when seen, it is red and black, and when it enters the skin, it looks like a white cord; then tie a thread tightly under it, so that it is raised from the skin, and then cut it at another place above three fingers; then open the skin over the wound so that it appears, then lift it to another hook, as you did before; then cut another incision, or several if you need to, then lift it and cut it at the toe of the foot, then pull and lift it up to the second incision; then draw it out from incision to incision, until it is all drawn out, then cut it; and if you cannot pull and lift it, then tie a strong double thread to a needle, and pierce and pull it, and tie it under the wound, and turn your hand from side to side, so that it comes out; and be careful not to burst it, because if it bursts, it cannot be pulled or lifted, and harm will come to the patient; and when you have treated it all, put on the wound a moistened woolen cloth with wine and rose oil; and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the vein is constricted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not cover it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron used to cover the vein is curved and does not cut so that it covers the vein; it has a large curve because if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but it should be large as we have said, and here is the shape:
de la voinne civile	of civil veins
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is winding in the legs, in warm parts where grass or trees do not grow, and in land without moisture; and by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the pus that comes under the skin, just as snakes and worms come inside the body, winding between skin and flesh.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a great swelling comes in the leg, then the place changes, and the vein begins to go out, as well as the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein is open, you should wrap it around with a piece of linen three and a half to four inches long, and the knot, and let the linen hang loose on the leg, and every time it comes out of its place, wrap it around the linen, and if it is too long, cut off a part, and wrap the rest, and do not cover it at all in its root, until it is all come out; for if you cover it, it will go back into the flesh, and cause an abscess and swelling in the place, and illness; therefore this vein should be treated little by little to the end, and nothing remain in the body; and sometimes this vein is as long as five or ten palms, and a man came to me once, from whom it issued ten palms long, and when you cover it, put in a reed or pipe, and pierce it to the bottom so that all of it comes out; and empty the matter which is inside, and bring medicine to the place to prevent swelling for several days, then cure it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes with this vein the hand bleeds, and especially when it opens at the joint of the foot, or in the foot, and there comes a lot of blood out, and from which it bleeds profusely; treat it therefore as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that live between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "cow disease" in our land because it often affects cows, and it is a small worm that lives between skin and flesh, moving throughout the body, going up and down, and can be felt as it moves from one part of the body to another until it breaks through the skin and emerges; it is caused by the putrefaction of certain humors, like worms, snakes, leeches, and roundworms in the belly; and it is feared for its malice, because when it moves through the body and reaches the head, it can enter and destroy the eye; this happens frequently.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and drawn out, it cannot be prevented except by waiting until it has drained; therefore, you must tie the area above and below with a strong string tightly, then press on top and draw it out forcefully; if the pus is deep in the flesh and you do not draw it out, cauterize it with fire until it comes to a head. The greatest harm it does is that it runs into the eye, as we have said; and if you see it coming near the eye, tightly constrict under it with a finger, then press on top and draw it out forcefully. It is necessary to use cleansing remedies for the body with dissolving medicines for the putrid humors, and cauterize with flesh-eating substances.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from flatulence
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vomiting" in our land, and it is a pain that affects some members, and then moves from one member to another; and I saw what I am telling you.
