Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman, and I uncovered her arm, and saw a small swelling on the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw it rising up as fast as a worm to the shoulder, quicker than anything else, as bright as silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain left that spot and went into the shoulder, and then a little later ran throughout the body, until it reached the other arm; then she said that she felt it turning around inside her body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very surprised how she moved from limb to limb like that, because I had never seen this disease progress in such a way before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I have seen many whose pain moves from one place to another, but not as I saw in this woman; and I thought it was because women's bodies are dry, and their veins exposed, and that this forced wind appears; and it does not appear in this way to those who are healthy, but to those with moist bodies and covered veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels that pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then ligature above and below firmly, and then compress gently until that forced wind is issued from its place; and cauterize the spot; and if you do not see it yourself, then treat it by those who dislodge the winds, as with foul pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearance and according to the place in the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	There are many types of stones: some have large, small, smooth, or pointed angles; some have two angles, some have tongues, and some have fragments. And when a stone falls into a limb, it falls in two ways: either into a principal member, such as the brain, heart, liver, lung, spleen, kidney, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When therefore she falls in any part of the body, and you see the signs of death which I shall tell you about later: then you must beware of extracting this arrow, for death comes afterwards in many cases; and when you do not see these evil signs, and the arrow is not deeply imbedded, draw it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the signs of the brain are when the arrow pierces the bone and reaches the brain, and there is a discharge of blood from the nose, and from the ears; and perhaps they lose their speech and voice; and there is white moisture like pus coming from the wound, and also bruising of the flesh; and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and disturbance of the mind, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is a discharge from the nose or ears; and perhaps they lose their speech and voice; and there is white moisture like pus coming from the wound, and also bruising of the flesh.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of a hernia when it occurs in the chest or abdomen are that it is located near the left breast, and feels as though it were pierced by a hard object, not hollow; and sometimes the hernia is silent like the pulse, and discharges black blood, and there is a chill and cold sweat, and a fainting: then know without doubt that death draws near.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow wound that pierces the lung is that without pain foam comes from the mouth, and the throat swells, and the patient's color changes, and they sigh deeply and seek the cold air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow pierces into the covering of the foot, it is located between the small ribs; and they spit up a lot of phlegm and experience great pain and sighing; and all their limbs move from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow hits the gut, by chance something indigestible might escape from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow hits the belly, and nothing comes out of the intestine but feces, then there is no hope for a cure, nor in extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow hits the bladder and urine escapes and comes out, and the patient feels great pain, know that the wound is lethal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face, neck, throat, shoulder, elbow, spine, hip, thigh, and leg, and similar members, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery and it is not venomous, as I will tell you so that you do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to a man that an arrow struck him in the jaw, near the root of the nose; I treated it, and drew it out from under the fat of the ear, and he was healed without any pain.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I treated a man who had an arrow that struck him in the fat of the eye below the eyelid, and the arrow was stuck, only the tip visible towards the nose; the arrow was as large as a Turkish bowstring, with a thin iron head; he was healed and no ill effects occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And I drew an arrow from the throat of a Christian, and it was an Arabic arrow to the ears; I lanced the abscesses, and I gently extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And I extracted an arrow from the liver of a man, who thought he would die; and after thirty days his condition did not improve; so I cut into the arrow, and removed it, and there was no bad outcome.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a man with an arrow in his back, and the wound is closed over it; and the arrow remains inside him, and his natural functions are not impaired, nor does he experience any discomfort in any of his natural processes.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man who had an arrow in his face, and the wound was closed over it; and he remained like that without experiencing great pain; and there are many other such cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I treated an arrow wound in the home of the prince, the king, which was lodged in his eye, and was slightly tilted to the right; and the arrow was completely removed. I was called to the cure after three days had passed.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I examined it with a subtle probe, and did not feel anything; but he felt pressure and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was the tip of the arrow. I placed a drawing and digestive poultice on the site to prevent swelling of the wound; and I saw the mark of the arrow.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I applied the poultice for several days, and the wound healed quickly, and the patient suffered for a long time, feeling the arrow in his eye for a day; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it opened, and I probed and felt the tip of the arrowhead underneath; then, using this medicine, I widened the opening of the wound until the head of the arrow became visible; and within four months, the wound healed well, and then I lanced the wound and pulled with tweezers from both sides but could not remove it; so I continued to treat it with various instruments until one day, using specially made tweezers, according to the method described at the end of this chapter, I extracted the arrowhead and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the doctor believed that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; so I restored it, and the wound was closed, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Now I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you put your care into what I do not say, for books cannot encompass everything; but wise masters consider well a very small thing, and what is present and lacking to them, they devise new works and new instruments, in the descent of strange things that come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows enter the body in two ways: either through the place where they entered or from another part; and those that exit through the place where they entered are arrows entering into fleshy parts, and sometimes they exit now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not exit right away, then leave it as long as the surrounding flesh is rotten and the exit is cleared; and also, if it is lodged in bone and cannot exit, then leave it for several days, moving it every day; and then it will exit, and if it doesn't, then pierce all around with a very thin needle until the surrounding area is widened, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the head, and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents that I have mentioned appear in the patient: then do not pull it out, but leave it until it is even after a few days, for if the arrow reaches the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not reach the brain, and the patient remains for several days without a bad accident, then treat it by pulling it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is lodged deeply and cannot be removed, then apply cauterization around the wound, as I have told you; then clean the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged deep in the body where you cannot see it, then explore all over its path; and if you feel it, pull it out with an appropriate instrument; but if because of the depth of the wound and the penetration of the arrow there is no bone or tendon or vein in the way, and if there is a great deal of flesh, then cut open the wound to the size of the arrow, and if there are any barbs on the arrow holding it in place, remove the surrounding flesh from both sides as much as you can, and then bend or fold back the barbs so that you can pull out the arrow; be careful not to break the arrow as you try to extract it.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot do this in one go, then leave it until the skin around it becomes toughened, and then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes you feel unwell, then do as we have said about the treatment in its chapter; and be careful not to cut the nerve or open a vein, and use whatever means you can to pull out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient as he was when the arrow struck him, for that is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot, then place him according to what the symptoms show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Arrows that come from another direction, or where something is protruding from them, or where the skin is swollen and it can be seen or felt: cut above, as far as the tweezers can reach, and then pull it out; if it will not come out now, try again later.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is stuck in the bone, then rotate your hand roundly, as far as it goes into the bone, and widen the hole, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it will not come out, then leave it and try again later; and if there is part of the arrow inside her, then remove it all; and if the shaft is broken, and you want to use leverage, then use a curved instrument so that the point of the arrow goes into the curve of the instrument; and then pull it out, and if the arrow is bent, place the instrument with its point entering inwards, to make the extraction easier.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow is touched, then you must cut away all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow pierces the buttocks or thigh or stomach or bladder or side, and it is close to the surface, and you can cut around it, then do so; but be careful not to cut into the vein or nerve, and then pull it out, and then stitch up the wound, if necessary; and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of tweezers used to treat arrow wounds is similar to an owl's beak; here is their shape:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrowhead.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of a broad-headed arrow is like the feather on an arrow, to push at the point of the arrowhead, just as it is shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape of the tongs to push and to pull it out if it is in there:
des voinnes dou cors communes	common body veins
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are thirty-one veins from which one recovers, and they have sixteen in the head, namely: two batons located behind the ears, called the "ear-veins"; and the two temples that are visible on the sides of the eyes, called the "temple-veins"; and the two veins in the eyelids above the eyes, called the "eyelid-veins"; and the vein in the forehead; and the vein at the base of the nose; and the two windpipes located at the back of the throat; and the two veins below the tongue. These are the veins known as the "gullet-veins".
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that are commonly used for bleeding are V in each arm: one is the cephalic, and it is on the left side, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called the "fast", and is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the cubital fossa, and it is the one that is used for bleeding, which opens clearly above the elbow.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatella is the vein that is between the auricular and annular, and it has II branches; and in the leg and foot there are III veins: one is below the bend of the pouch on the left side, and the second sophene which is at the ankle on the right side; and the vein that is called  "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are III veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of veins that are behind the ears is helped by old cathartic remedies, and by emigration; and the qualities of the sanguinary, as I have told you, and it is that you raise the head of the patient, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then press the patient's neck to a pulse, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places, depending on the head; then sign with your finger, and where you feel the pulse under your finger, press inward; then take the lance, and pierce beneath the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand to the entire vein upstream, and cut through both the skin and the vein thoroughly for a distance of two fingers, and make the blood flow until you see it; then press and ligature it, until it is healed; and I have already spoken of the incision and cautery in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries in the temples is useful for treating ancient migraine, and sore eyes and habitual blindness, and tears in the body of the eye; and the quality of the bleeding is as I have said: and it makes the patient turn his neck so that the two veins are clearly visible; then he feels pain under his toe, and then signs himself with his hand; then he applies the hot stone above the vein on his finger, and inserts the lance below, and opens the vein above, and draws out the blood according to his need; then he releases the patient, and puts his finger on the vein for an hour, then cotton; and then binds it up firmly, and leaves it until it is healed; and we have already spoken of their binding and extraction in the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding from the vein in the forehead is as effective as the bleeding from the cephalic vein for old diseases of the face, and for migraines and redness; and the qualities are such that the patient turns his neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", of which here is the shape:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point over the vein, and press gently with your hand or something else, and let the blood flow according to the amount you see; then release the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed, and sometimes the operation can be done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flames should not be too hot; and the sick person is crooked, for the bone is close by, and perhaps the flames will break when they are thin.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding from the two veins that are in the jaw helps with teeth, and with tinea, and redness, and with a stye in the eye, and with diseases of the face; and the qualities of their bleeding are such that the patient turns his neck by twisting some ligament, as before; then bleed him, and the bleeding should be across the vein, a little from the long flame, a little wide, because there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, they may break; then draw blood from it, as much as you need, and then bind it with a thread, and tie it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The bleeding of the vein is good for ague, and for sudden frenzy, and for diseases of the face, such as migration and redness that comes to the face, and also when it is old; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient squeezes his throat, then pulls out his nose with your left hand, and takes a long, slender flame, and inserts it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well there, and the blood will begin to flow now; and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then ligate it overnight, for it is quickly restored. And this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The bleeding of the two veins helps with strangulation of the larynx, and with the beginning of hoarseness, and many diseases, and with impetigo, and with scurvy, and with herpes, and with ulcers; and the quality of the bleeding is that the patient squeezes his throat under one or both armpits, as we have said; and let the master stand over the patient's head, and the patient sit on a chair, then bleed the vein on the neck widely for a short time, then draw the blood gently, as needed; then do the same in the other vein, then loosen the ligature, and squeeze both veins gently so that the patient does not choke; and let him be until the morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	of bleeding from the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Bleeding from the veins of the lips helps with sores in the mouth and gum corruption and lip splits and toothaches.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the nature of the bleeding is to have the patient sit before you and strain his neck as I have said; then turn the lip and look at the two veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which can be recognized because they are black, and because there are small black veins around them: compress both, and if you do not recognize them and you are in doubt, then compress the largest of each side, and likewise do the same with the two veins above and below, for it is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of bleeding under the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bleeding of veins that are underneath the tongue is helped after the bleeding of the cephalic vein; and it is in the constriction of the throat, and in diseases of the eye, and in diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the bleeder is such that the patient feels faint between his hands in front of the sun, and he lightens the tongue, and looks under each side for a black vein: therefore heal one and the other, and do not go too deep, for underneath are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck from which one usually bleeds are healed in two ways: either with a large mirtin flame, or an olive-shaped one as thin as a needle, and is called 'anesil'; and they are large and thin according to the width and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the mortar is highly renowned, and it is wide as you can see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open wide veins that are filled with thick and apparent blood, and which contain thick and troubled blood; and this is the shape of the olive-shaped flame:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and refined, and is used for bleeding subtle veins, where there is thin and yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps diseases that are under the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the belly; and the surgeon must cut it bleeding, and cauterize the artery underneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he cuts the artery and bleeding ensues, it must be staunched as I have said; and the flame should not be held, but cut like a bridle.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilic does not open clearly, then you must probe it and change to another vein; or you can take a vein from him in his arm: it will open clearly; and you cut it with the flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the location of the vein, you must stretch out the arm and feel the pulse; then mark the spot on the inside, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with the flame, as we have said; and be careful not to cut into the artery when you see the spot is swollen, for it is the artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rising up like a child's urine, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is arterial blood: therefore, hurry and put your finger on it for a long time, then take away your finger if the blood stops, which often happens; tie the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; and let him be in fear, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if the blood is staunched, and he vomits, and the medicine is not present, then press on the artery until it is closed, and stop the flow of blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	Take a piece of oak bark, and split it, and take one half and tie it on well until the next day; if the blood stops, that is good; if not, then treat it as we have said with powders that stop bleeding; and the stopping of the blood is not harmful in many conditions because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The bleeding from the vein is helped by its being opened from above and from below, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic veins, as we have said; and the bleeder must be careful not to pierce too deeply, and to find the vein, and if it swells and the wound is enlarged, and by chance cannot heal; and this vein often opens, and in some men does not open because of its subtlety, so you should bleed it with a sharp instrument, and cut the vein as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, they will cut it through the long one.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The bleeding from the cephalic vein is helped by its being opened from above and from below; and one should bleed it with a flame of olive oil or of myrtle, for this is the safest of all veins, for there are no nerves or arteries beneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, one must seek the lightest place, and if one fails the first time, one must try again; and by chance, some men swell up where they fail the first time, but it does them no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the cautery depends on your skill.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is only done to maintain health and prevent future illnesses; bleeding should be performed in one of the three veins: the cephalic, the fast, and the basilic; bleeding should be done at the beginning of lent, in autumn and winter after eating when the signs of digestion are apparent; and one should bleed on the first or third day after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Bleeding that is administered for illnesses does not have a set time, but whenever the need arises during the day or night, in all hours and at any time; one should not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor should pregnant women be bled after the fourth month until the seventh month.Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should the very old who have passed 60 years be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when anyone wishes to bleed themselves, in whatever manner, they should first evacuate the bowels with a gentle enema if they have retained much feces, so that the veins do not draw harmful excess fluids from the intestines into the principal limbs; nor should one bleed those who are bloated from eating too much meat, or who are drunk, until some time has passed, or those who are suffering from dropsy. And one should not bleed after a colic attack, vomiting, diarrhea, or excessive sexual intercourse with a woman, or from exertion, watching all night, or fasting; rather, subtly reduce the humors through food and drink, if you have the skill; then enter the bath to subtlety the blood, and bleed from the arm vein around the bend of the elbow on the third day, as we have said; and guard against exertion, puncturing, and luxury that day; and be calm and cheerful, and let the person bleeding be higher than the one being bled, and stroke their arm two or three times; then tighten the ligature above the vein gently, for if it is too loose or too tight, it will not work; then stroke the area with your hands until the veins swell and are felt; then moisten the bleeding person's arm with a little old oil, then place the tip of their left hand on that vein below the spot where they want to bleed, so that the vein does not slip away from the needle.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow as strings do in a bowstring, and some are filled with wind so that when one applies flame to them, they withdraw from the flame and cannot open the vein; thus it is with these. And if one opens the vein, then the wound is too narrow for this, so it behooves that surgeons be skilled in such matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein works the first time, that is good; if not, do it again a little lower down at the same spot or above, if the area isn't swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the vein is swollen and the patient is afraid, if you leave it for one or two days and do not bind the arm, perhaps an abscess will form; nor should he enter the bath, but resume bleeding if it pleases him; and if the opening is small, insert a thin blade into the vein and apply flame directly to the opening; and work gently and quickly so that the vein swells; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the wound is swollen, do not restart the bleeding, and put a little liniment of oil on it, because it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the liniment of oil; and thus administer the liniment of oil in every wound that you bleed the veins, to stop the flow of blood; and this same thing does triacle and bowels do when they are put on the spot; they subtly draw out the blood when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, especially when it is not bled except for that once when the opening of the vein is small, you must hurry and put a sponge moistened with warm water on the spot and hold it there for an hour; and you must do this after the flow of blood from the wound, and if it remains in place for some days and a blackness or greenness appears, it does not matter; and if you see it, put something made into a ointment of aloe or myrrh.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there occurs an abscess and appearance at the exit of the vein: therefore place your hand upon it, and if you find the spot soft to the pressure of your hand, then is that appearance evil.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore beware that you do not place anything of what we have said upon it, for perhaps it pierces through an artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the spot, then treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each wound according to its quantity and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and swollen, and needs bloodletting, that one makes a larger wound on him, and the flames should be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and one should bleed them a little and often, and one should bleed them by cutting diagonally, not by piercing; and this method of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and it is better than bleeding from a long or wide cut.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body needs bleeding, it is good to give them wet bread in pomegranate juice; if they are feverish, then eat it three or four times before the bleeding. And if of a cold complexion, then eat wet bread in rosewater syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chives, and very fragrant syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints at the bleeding, after the loss of much blood, then one should drink a mixture of meat broth and subtle fragrant syrup, and use other things that we have said in the division of syncope, for the opening of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to empty his arm and bleed again, it is necessary that when he is weakened by a great bleeding, that he bleeds a little at a time according to the amount of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And he who wishes to open his arm after the first bleeding, and has strong pulse, should bleed seven hours after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wishes to bleed elsewhere, should do so on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For he has much blood inside his body which is now scorched, and it brings on fever; so one must draw out a great quantity, and widen the vein until it bleeds freely; then you should check all the conditions of bleeding, and put your hand over his pulse while he bleeds, so that death does not come in the place of fainting, and this happens many times when the surgeon is negligent; and one must not press hard on the vein when it has bled a second time and is closed, or if it is crooked, stretch out the arm forcefully, for that would be bad; but let it bleed until it heals a second time; or touch it with the tip of a flaming torch, so that the congealed blood at the opening of the vein melts, and put a little vinegar in water on it, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, leave it and don't constrict it at all until the abscess is drained.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to let blood a second time, then bleed in the same vein, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arms are healthy in the area of the vein in the head because it is compound.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the way to heal it is for the patient to put his hand in hot water until the vein turns red; then let him be bled slightly, so that the vein appears well, then heal it now from the center, not from the side or the end; and let the incision be wide, and let it be healed close to the joint of the hand, and if it cannot come out, put the hand back in hot water and let the blood run into the water until you have enough; and if it is winter, do not put the hand back in hot water, because it is put in more in winter than in summer; and the healing of this vein is safer than all other veins, for there is no artery or nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The healing of the save-the-right-hand vein is good for all diseases of the liver, and this is how: straighten the hand, and put it in hot water until the vein is swollen; and if you see the vein, then heal it from the center, and if you cover it completely, then it will not hurt; and do not go too deep, because the nerves are all stripped of flesh underneath, and then put the hand back in hot water if the blood is frozen in the wound and cannot come out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have stopped the bleeding as much as is necessary, then put oil and silk on the vein to stop it, and do this for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is beneficial for the disease of the mouse, and do everything just as I told you about the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The medicine of the sophia is good for all diseases that are under the body, such as diseases of the stomach, and retention of fluid, and diseases of the intestines, and the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its medicine are such that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it breaks, and applies it to the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and up the foot they go a lot of veins; therefore heal them at the widest vein, or at the ankle, whichever is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you cut it off at the foot, then guard against the nerves underneath, and cut it through horizontally as well as vertically; and let the flames be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot come out, then put the foot in water and let the vein empty well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the medicine does not work the first time, try it again the second time higher up, because the place is salty; do not worry about nerves, as we have said, and similarly make sophia of the other foot in the same way.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle, and its pulsation indicates the pain in the hip, when it is due to hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the nature of its healing is that the patient enters the bath, and twists above the ankle IIII turns, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then heal it in every way you can, and by twisting; and it is better that you close it, for the place is safe, and it is very relaxed in many people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not twist it, then heal any vein that opens on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and watch out for the nerves; and make the blood flow until you see it, and then untie the ligature, and put on cotton and press it; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of cupping
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Leeches are made of horns, or brass, or glass; and bloodletting is done in two ways: by striking and drawing blood, or without striking.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping that is without heat is done in two ways: with or without fire; and cupping which is done by cauterization and by the extraction of blood is performed in 14 places on the body, one of which is at the top of the head; and another is in the neck; and two others are on either side of the neck; and a cupping glass under the chin; and cupping glasses on the two shoulders; and cupping glasses over the hips; and cupping glasses in the two arms; and cupping glasses in the two legs; and cupping glasses at the ankles; and cupping does not draw blood, except for tiny veins that are scattered in the flesh, and because of this it weakens them in no way, as is done with vein-cutting; and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without, in any disease that comes from repletion, until the whole body has been emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	If, due to illness or habit, one must bleed, then we let them bleed every hour at the beginning or end of the month, and during the night and day; for there are those who, when they need to bleed, feel a heavy head, and some experience bloating and redness in their face, head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and some have a drop of blood in their mouth, and their tongue swells, and they taste blood.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, especially if they occur during the month, we command them to fast after the third hour of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The bleeding of the nose helps with headaches ... that come to the eyes, and it must not be after the evacuation of the whole body; and this venting is in the place of the bleeding of the cephalic, and it must not be used by those who are of a cold complexion, or who have catarrh, for it does them great harm; and for this reason, the elderly should not use it, nor those with cold diseases in their heads.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who recover from it often become oblate, and for this reason one should place the cupping glass a little lower down in case of oblateness.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation in the neck is in the location of the jugular vein and the basilic vein, and because of this, it helps with constriction of the feet, and with fissures in the channels of the lungs, and with vomiting and distension; and one must not press on it too much, for if it is held too tightly, it causes damage to the throat, stomach, and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilation at the two sides of the neck helps with headaches, and blindness and weeping eyes, and strangulation, and pain in the roots of the teeth, and is located where the basilic vein is; and one must instruct the patient to express their hand while putting it on, so that they do not compress the artery and cause blood to flow.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Winding pains below the chin cause mouth disease and gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the place of bleeding from the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Winding pains in the shoulders cause disease that comes from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilation in the armpits is like three veins in the arm, for it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient not to press too hard, for the area is bare of flesh, and underneath are nerves and arteries.Li ventosations de la pethe si vaut a la sainie dou pormon, et a estrecement des cotes, et a dolors del costel, et a sainie des os; et covient que tu commandes au sainor qu’il ne fière mie par la voinne, car s’il le fist, il velt la pethe.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass placed on the buttocks is good for hemorrhoids and diseases underneath; it should be large, made of copper, and well-suctioning; and if it were thin, it could break and cause large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The leg cupping glasses heal very effectively, for they draw blood from the entire body and are good for old pains in the hips, and the joints of the loins, and the bladder, and draw out humours; and are placed over the two sciatic nerves, and over the two ankles, and yet they weaken the body after long use, and bring fainting in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method for applying the cupping glass is that you place it first empty, and suck gently, and press firmly, and move equally, and do not stop doing so until you see the area red and swollen, and the redness of the blood appears; then stop, and remove the cupping glasses, and take care in the disposition of the body, for there are those who have very thin skin and clear pores; therefore one must strike only once, and one must make wide wounds, and a little deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, then it is necessary to strike twice: the first time to open the path of the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, then it is necessary to strike a third time; and when we want to draw little by little, we only need to strike once.Et se li sans est gros et espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois, et la quarte.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If we want to draw a lot of blood, we should make incisions often; if the blood is thick, pierce it with a needle, and if the skin is tough and hard, with narrow pores, one should anoint the places where the cupping glasses will be placed, with an aperitif and dissolving oil: if the patient is in good health, with violet oil, or with sweet almond oil, or with squash seed oil; and if they are pale, with watercress oil, or lily of the valley oil, or camomile oil, or something similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, then take oil of marjoram, or of balsamite, or of fennel, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if they have soft skin and large pores, one should not put any oil on them, but rather wash with rosewater, or cold water, or mulberry water, or squash water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture should get up from garlic, or myrrh water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those with large sores should rise from old wine, or water of sugar, or a decoction of aniseed or camomile, or other similar remedies; and one should not bleed by leeches before the bath or in the bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and one should not sleep after being bled, and it is necessary that he should warm himself when he is to be bled and when he has been bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And watch that the patient is not choleric, and that the blood is not too thin and inflamed; then he should eat cool foods such as pomegranates, endives and lettuce with garlic, and similar things; and soft foods like purées, and porridge, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those with a cool complexion should drink honey syrup and medium-old sweet wine, and eat soft foods like purées and porridge, and small birds and pigeons; and on the day he is bled, he should drink more than he eats; and it is good to give some men triacle or musk before or after bleeding to comfort the principal members; and the blood must be subtle but those with a hot complexion should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses that are placed without breaking the skin are those that are placed on the liver, and on the mumps, and on the gout, and on the belly, and the groin, and the ribs, and the hip, because these members do not bear being pierced with holes, and it is only done to draw blood from one member to another, as we do when we put them on the breasts when the nipples are healthy; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we do when we place cupping glasses on the belly and the groin to reduce the size of the member; and it takes away pain when there is inflammation or a stone, and by its attractive power it may draw out the inflammation, or dislodge the stone from its place; and thus it acts when one applies it to the liver and the mumps when there is retained wind, and these cupping glasses are administered empty merely to suck; and sometimes they are applied with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in this way one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been boiled.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the fire cupping instrument is as follows:
