Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	It is two digits wide and half a palm deep, and on the side near the middle it has a small hole, just big enough to push through an awl, made of bronze or iron so that it does not hurt the patient when placed over the affected limb; and in the middle there is a crossbar made of bronze or iron, to hold a candle, and they are larger or smaller depending on the illness and the age of those who use them, for the ventouses used on children are different from those used on the old, and those used on the thin are different from those used on the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And thus one must apply this ventouse to the affected limb: take a candle made of wax or tallow, and place it inside the ventouse so that its flame is at the bottom of the ventouse and does not burn the patient; then apply it to the limb, and hold your fingers over the hole we mentioned, so that when you wish, the vapors may escape, and remove the ventouse. Then take the tallow as before and reapply it frequently if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the cupping glass therefore which is administered for the disease of pleurisy, has no pipe nor hole, and is not released until it is full of water, and is placed on the limb only; and that is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are not released until in members where one cannot place cupping glasses due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in bare flesh, such as testicles or nipples, and others; and the quality of using them is that when you find leeches that are in clear, clean water without any dirt, take them; and put one needle into clear water, so that they become accustomed and do not move in their bellies; then heal with a vein-opening and cupping, then rub the member until it turns red, and place the leeches on top of it; and when they are full and start to bleed, if there is a place where one can place a cupping glass, do so, for that is much better.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then raise the area with ash, and then with water, very well, and then squeeze it out; and if the vein bleeds too much after the body of the leeches, then moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and place it over the wound until the bleeding stops; and if the bleeding is profuse, then apply crushed vitriol, or gales, and similar things, until it is stopped; or you can place half a handful of peeled peas over the area, and leave them until they turn dry on the spot, and it will stop the bleeding now; and if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches will not attach, then rub the bleeding area with fresh blood, or you can insert a needle into the vein and then place them over it, and as soon as they feel the blood, they will attach; and when you see that they are defecating, then sprinkle on some powdered aloe and ashes, or cinder, and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is a cure for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish men who wrote this chapter never saw any of the ancient books, nor did they read them; and for this reason, knowledge is strange in our land, for I have never found any good ones; and I know nothing about them except through the knowledge of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have learned their science, and through experiment and the habit of my life. And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained in it, and have abbreviated it at the end, and have clearly shown the forms of the instruments used, as I have done in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say in the prologue of this book about the matters contained within, and the chapters where the sage sets his understanding, and dwells upon truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a break or dislocation or twisting or crushing occurs in someone, you must hurry to heal the patient from one side and the other, if nothing else prevents it, such as weakness of the body, or a fever, or old age; or if the weather is not very hot, or too cold; and eat cool foods, that is, cool birds and kid meat, and do not drink any wine, nor eat any fatty foods, and do not fill yourself too much with meat that fills the veins with blood, until you have a doubt about a hot abscess or the spreading of matter in the limb; then return the patient to their first treatment.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, one should nourish the patient with foods that promote swelling, or have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, rice, testes, feet, pig's belly, offal, freshwater fish, and full-bodied wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	Because with more swelling, the break will heal faster.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well healed or united according to their nature because of the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but have no worry, reset the broken bone, pulling on the large tendons that extend and join the limb together, as tightly as it was before; and do not stop at any point in his work, and because of this one should eat plenty of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are diverse in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the head is different from the fracture of the foot, or of the leg, and I will tell you in this chapter about all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	Because there is a fracture which goes towards the root, and another in sharpening, as with the tip of a writing quill.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a break with a wound, and a break throughout a small split.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And in each way it has its own art and proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory comes into his mind; and the fracture of the bone is known by the fact that the joint is twisted, and clearly appears by feeling, and sounds on being pressed with the hand; and when there is no twisting or pain on touch, but the patient feels no great pain, then there is no fracture; but there may be a dislocation, or split, or small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You must not move it with your hand, but apply remedies that are described below, and then hold it steady with a gentle grip.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture which goes in the bone, and are the two parts separated, they must now be put back together evenly, so that abscesses heal; and if cold abscesses come, he leaves it for a day, until the abscesses are healed; then he puts it equal to the movement that you can leicht and gently, and know that the restoration of which is easier than the restoration of one where there are pieces; then he tightens, as it should be done hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, whether it is in the hand or foot, or to your hand if it is a small member, or to two tendons, or one tendon and your hand; and put the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, he pulls by all means the additions into their places as you can, and guard so that by your work does not come to the patient injury or pain; and fit well the two heads of the bone according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	Feel it with your hand to see if it is not in the right position; then adjust it properly and do not strain or press too hard as those do who cause hot abscesses and contraction of the limb through their treatment, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is ready, then treat the patient carefully so that he does not move it, whether waking or sleeping, turning or otherwise; and be sure to keep the limb so secure that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, it is not yet healed, and you must put him in such a position that he feels no pain; and be careful that it is set aright, so that no crookedness comes to it when it is restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members vary in size, shape, and form.Les quels conviennent a l’un et ne conviennent pas a l’autrier;
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small limbs, such as arms and fingers and the like: these should be wrapped in soft, fine linen; and for larger ones, such as thigh and leg: these should be wrapped with a wide, strong bandage, because wide bandages embrace the entire large limb and constrict it evenly from all sides, so that there is no swelling; then wind lightweight linen or cloth around it three or four times according to the size of the limb, and press your hand firmly on the bandage all around, then go above the fracture and constrict less, so that the fracture is drawn out a little; then soften the bandage little by little, until you grasp most of the healthy part, then take another bandage and wind it around directly over the broken part; then go to the part below the fracture and constrict gently, neither too hard nor too soft, as we have said above in the first hour; then put between the bandages linen or cloth, so that they are all even, then bind everything above with a bandage, and then put your splints well-made on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, then place something hot to soothe the abscess and reduce the swelling, leaving it like that for a few days; then press down on the teeth, which should be made from half a piece of split cane, or from wood used for making clefts, or from palm wood, and they should be shaped thus:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but the tooth that is placed on the break should be a little bigger and wider than the others; it should also be as long as the member needs to be short or long; then press down on the teeth as you did at first, then tie a thread over it appropriately, just as in the first instance on the break; the tighter it is, the better; and the thread should be fine, not too coarse or too fine, and it should be made of soft flax; for if the threads are coarse, as I have seen fools do when they make their ligatures with tightly twisted cords, that is a great mistake, for the ligature cannot be equal if it is too fine, and there should not be less than a finger's width between each tooth.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is raw under the eyes of the stars after the straining in their healthy state, then place underneath them lint or woolen rags so that it does not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture and the skin is broken, I will describe its treatment below.Car li grant maladous que l’on dit estre de la piere ne sont pas touz si de la piere; mes de la briseure qui adont la piere, et del chié qui de la briseure adont la plaie; si est li granz maux, et la grant piere ne se peut guérir si l’on n’estranche la piere.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not appropriate to dislocate all broken limbs on the first day.Car li maux adont les membres par la briseure, et la piere que adont la plaie, il covient li premier jor estraindre li maux de la piere, et le second jor esguarer li maux del chié; car il ne doit guérir li maux de la piere li premier jor, mes li autrez joures.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the member is large, you should not put splints on it for more than five or seven days, or longer depending on the heat of the abscess; and here is the way of the ancient plasters to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: You take the flour that is left on the walls of the mill, cook it with plenty of egg, and apply this mixture, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common way of the plaster that restores fractures in various conditions, especially in women and young children, because it is not too hot or too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of plaster restoring the fracture and dislocation and twisting: take 3 grains of barley and ladani and ennule and asafetida and gum arabic and mastic, each 10 grains; myrrh and aloes, each 5 grains; alechil 8 grains; and make them into powder, and mix them with plenty of egg; if the complexion of the man is hot, use this plaster, because it is of good composition, and restores broken bones quickly, and is useful to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of plaster that is good for twists: take mastic and balm of gilead, each 10 grams; myrrh and aloes, each 8 grams; aqua armena, 6 grams; and grind well, and cook with water or plenty of egg, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of plaster for joints and bones that have become dislocated from their sockets, and to ease the resulting pain, and to treat fractures: take new linen and soak it in lard and cooked oil, then apply it to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not heal, but it is good for soothing hot abscesses and easing pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of poultice that heals broken bones: take dry fig leaves and dead nettle leaves, crush them together, and make a poultice.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plaster to heal fractures and reduce swelling from an abscess.Take the yolk of a hard-boiled egg, and mix it with vinegar until it becomes thick like honey, then add powdered herbs, and apply it to the affected area.This plaster is good for healing fractures and reducing pain and swelling.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of marshmallow, chamomile, violet flowers, and wheat flour, one part each; grind them and mix with wine to form a paste. If the affected area is hot, then mix the paste with coriander water or regular water and apply it.This plaster is good for healing fractures and reducing pain and inflammation.Take the yolk of a hard-boiled egg, and mix it with vinegar until it becomes thick like honey, then add powdered herbs, and apply it to the affected area.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method of ointment stronger than the first, when a hard abscess comes to the restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of marshmallow, and flax seed, comfrey, and myrrh, and flowers of violets and chamomile; of each take one part. Grind them and cook in water with salt, or fresh water, or wine, depending on the heat of the limb and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypocrites says in his book that one should not put anything on a broken member to heal it other than a ointment made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says it should be between soft and too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen says one should put on the broken member, to heal, dry things a little warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another type of ointment that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and shaved human hair, or bird feathers, and bee wax, and mix them together, and grind them up, and make an ointment from it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little after, and be careful that the patient does not feel any pain, nor move the bone from its place; if not, loosen it after several days. And if pain comes to the site, or itching, without rest or swelling, hurry and loosen it, and remove the ointment immediately; take a light cloth, and sponge of sea moisture, and dip in water, and lift the site until the itching stops and the pain is relieved; then let the limb rest for an hour, then place a wet linen moistened in water or rose oil, and bind upon a nut, until you are sure there is no hot abscess; and the inflammation of the limb will subside, and the pain will be removed, then begin the binding gently again, and a little ointment, and do not tighten it as much as before; and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that there is heat and redness and pain and swelling still remaining in the body, and you need ointment and binding, then restart it, just as you did at first.Et se tu vois que li membre est sane et apaisie, si le tiens en repos et en legier cheis, et ne le deffait mie tant qu’il ne soit tout sanz dolor; et tu tiens li membre ou il doit estre, si com tu avies fait premierement.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If the limb does not receive anything of what we have said, do not dislocate it until three or four or five or seven days; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, according to what one sees, as long as the fracture heals, and the joint approaches the bone underneath; then restrain it more than before, and increase his food, as I have said before; and if you see the site drier than is necessary, know that nourishment cannot come there; therefore soak it with warm water every time you dislocate it, and do this every third day, and loosen the bandage a little; through this work, nourishment reaches the limb, and quickly corrects what the foolish healers do, who restore the limb crookedly: this is bad, and such work is cowardly, and I see nothing in it but laziness and doing it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many types of fractures, with different shapes and distinct causes. Some fractures are caused by the impact of a sword, breaking the collarbone all the way to the hip, as happens with an axe or a pole; this type of fracture is called a "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword strikes the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and the wound of these two fractures are great or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is concussion accompanied by swelling, or fracture, or a blow from a stone, or falling on a stone, or similar.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a fracture penetrating to the membrane just under the bone, or on top of the bone; and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is repented in the bone as thin as a hair, and the crack is small, then this type of fracture is called  "capillary". And if the wound is caused by a stone, or by falling, or by a similar object, and the bone fragment enters below, and the site is smooth like the smiths when they work on kettles; then the bone is split.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more to those with soft bones in the head, like the heads of children; and it happens with all types of fractures where small pieces are dislodged, as with tiles; I will speak about them in their place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we should know all types of fractures through examination, and through the corrupt flesh that is on top of it.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known by this: when one uncovers the bone and rubs it gently, then the fracture appears black.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of a fracture, pay attention to any bad signs of illness, and if you see any harmful incidents, such as vomiting bile, loss of consciousness, seizures, feverish shivering, eyes bulging and turning red, and other similar symptoms in various conditions, then it cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see any shocking incidents and you expect a recovery, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the patient first comes to you and it is winter, then you should remove the splint before the fourteenth day of the month that you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the spring, then you should hasten to remove the splint before the seventh day so that the flesh underneath the bone does not rot and cause the incidents we have described.The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	If the fracture of the bone comes just to the membrane that covers the brain, then you should split the split part thus: and it is that you press the head of the wound, and expose on the bone in all the ways you can, and over the shape of the wound more gently than you can, and if bleeding occurs when exposing the bone, or a hot abscess, use aid as appropriate, and fill the site with soft rags moistened in rosemary oil; let the wound rest until the hot abscess is soothed, and make sure there is no further bleeding; then start around the bone to remove it, and this is done according to two methods of work: one method is that you cut straight ahead with a small knife, and this is the shape:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then put another cut larger than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second manner is that you have a number of diverse tools, some narrow and others wide, and are pointed, and made of iron; and work gently so that you do not blister the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, you must pierce it around, so that you administer tools with chisels, not deeper than to penetrate through the bone of the skull, and it should have above the point a rim or .i. circle, which does not let the point pass through the bone; and you should have several of these, so that each one comes in its place in the thickness of the bone, so that you have chisels for all skulls; and this is the form of the .iij. ways of chisels:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing around the broken bone is to put .i. chisel on the bone, and turn with your fingers until you know that the bone is pierced; then put the chisel elsewhere a little later, and thus do all around, then cope with the incisions the space of the bone which is between the holes, and do this most subtly and gently, as we have said, so that you draw out the bone to your hand, or to any of the instruments you have, such as tweezers, pincers; and beware of touching the brain or the membrane.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and cut the bone, it is appropriate to resect the membrane that is remaining on the bone with any other similar instrument like an incision tool, but it must be more blunt and thinner than the other incision tools; and if anything of the small bones or scales remain, remove them lightly with the instruments; then treat the wound with tenting and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other method of treatment is that which Galen describes, which is safer; and he praises it highly, and his words are as follows:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First, you must expose a part of the bone where the open fracture is located; then, once that part is exposed, place under the head of this lens-shaped instrument, of which this is the shape:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side, and the part is pain in both sides, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then hit with a small mallet above, so that you gently kop the bone all around, and be careful of the membrane that is underneath; if it is adhered to the bone, then loosen it slightly, for the bone can be loosened without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not penetrate to the membrane, and the bone is only cut slightly on top, and there are small pieces, then you should smooth that roughness, and remove the scales with a very thin razor, of which you should have various quantities, in order to apply the most suitable one in each place, according to the action and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	Take first a large razor, and then a thinner one, and do not cease doing this until it is smooth.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hairline fractures and delicate breaks, you should apply treatment according to their nature; and this is something that is not laid out for one who has dedicated his study to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is exposed, you should take a piece of linen according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another double piece of linen, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first piece of linen; and do this as gently as you can so that you do not put pressure on the sinus, then administer medicine afterwards through another opening, and do not pull harder than just to touch the wound; and leave it like this for one or two days, until the abscess is relieved, then loosen it, and apply medicine such as linden roots, and flour of beans, and incense powder, and aristology, and similar things; and make a powder from these things, and place it over the wound, and administer medicine without biting; and be careful that the wound is clean, so that you do not leave any ointment on it, nor let any pus collect under the membrane of the brain, for when pus collects there, it causes great harm to the patient.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care then, if no ill accident comes to the patient, as we have said, for it is certain without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness does not come from the medicine that one has put on it, for such virtue that it has, then you must take a part of honey and three parts of rose oil and glue a cloth to it; then treat it with treatment methods as is appropriate, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the jaw above are broken, either by themselves or together, for they are two bones; and below is cartilage, which does not break but only bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should boil your little finger or a needle, and place the break inside your index finger, and hold it in place with your thumb, until the nail grows back to its natural shape; do this lightly, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your treatment.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the break is in the part above the nail, and cannot come to the place of the finger, then you must put it equally at the top of a piece of wood, rather thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is in two parts, do this likewise, and try to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses are healed, then boil a tent of linen cloth around the nail if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you attach another from another part, if the fracture is there; and let the tents be so thick that they fill the openings of the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one must soak the tents in butter and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that this is good, but one should soak the bandages in egg white and flour; then leave the bandage as long as the bone is broken, and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes they attach goose feathers instead of tents, and wrap it in a silk cloth, and keep the fracture still, and the patient breathes through it; do as you like.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if painful abscesses come in the nose while you are working on it, then apply cerot or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a little dyer's alkanet.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses form, then apply a poultice of wheat flour and incense powder, infused with egg white, then place light bandages on top, but do not tie them too tightly; and if the fracture is small, and it is broken into tiny pieces, then extract it with suitable instruments, cleaning and closing the wound with warm, soothing ointments and poultices, as appropriate for such injuries; and if there is no wound inside the ear, then treat it with bandages, and apply canes of lead until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	of the dislocation of the jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated below and there is no wound in evidence, and only the joint is dislocated without fracture, and not broken in two, so that it is bent inside, one can perceive this easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the dislocation is on the right side, you should insert your right index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if it is on the left side, insert the right index finger and gently push the joint back into place with the other hand, keeping it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the dislocation of the jaw is dislocated to one side, one should administer an extension of two parts, so that it becomes even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement in the teeth, or a fracture, then bind them with a gold or silver wire, or silk; then apply cerate to the broken mandible, and place a double drape over it; and place a large, well-made splint, or a piece of equal leather, long and wide according to the mandible, and tie it in place as tightly as possible; and instruct the patient to rest, and eat soft foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the jaw is changing shape, then loosen it on the third day, and then put it back into place again; and apply ointment over it, made of powdered millstone with egg white or flour, after you have removed the cerate; and place a thin layer of lamb's wool over the ointment, and if the jaw is not healing, and its condition remains unchanged, leave it as long as necessary until it heals, sometimes within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if a hot abscess comes, then administer what we have said many times.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, examine it to see if any piece of bone has been displaced; then reset it with suitable instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces and nothing remains inside, then stitch the wound, if it is wide, and place upon it suitable poultices to promote healing, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the armpit
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The armpit may break in many ways towards the shoulder, and there are three types of breaks: it may be broken and displaced in two places with pieces, which is the easiest to heal; or it may be broken with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the work is when there is no wound in the fracture, that you have two ministers, so that one holds the shoulder which feels the broken collarbone; and the other stretches the neck towards the part; then put the break equal in your hands, so that it has neither appearance nor swelling.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you need to extend more, then put under the shoulder of the patient a round piece of cloth, or of woolen cloth, and let it be thick according to your need; and they lift and loosen the collarbone, and hold the cloth in your hand, so that you make the break even, as it should be.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the collarbone out of its socket because it is deeply embedded, then the patient should lie on his back, and put under the shoulder a small pillow, and the ministers press the shoulder down, until the bone of the collarbone is raised up.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then grasp the break with your hands, and if you find it split, then you must split it open; and gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot join because of any swelling, then use this instrument to ward off the skin:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	it resembles a spoon, and is not hairy, and is as wide as it needs to be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and it has two heads, as you can see, and one is wide, and the other narrow, as is the shape of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of a hot abscess, cut the wound, and if the channel is small, or if you doubt the hot abscess, apply the wound with bandages and tenting, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, then moisten a piece of linen in rosemary oil and garlic and wine, and place it over the wound.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The stretching of the bone, when there is no wound or fracture, is to place on the bone the poultice of mill-dust and egg white, and place light dressings over it, and put a small sponge under the joint, if you need it; then take a very large band one palm wide, then place a doubled cloth over the dressings and poultice; then take a slender staff three fingers wide and long, and wrap it around that band so that the head of the band hangs down; and place the staff over the fracture, and wind the band around the neck, and under the healthy shoulder blade, and under the sick shoulder blade; and adjust each part, and when you see that the binding holds the fracture in place, and you clearly see that the staff does not move on the broken bone, then reward it every day, and when the ligature becomes loose, tighten it; and make the patient lie on his back, and put a small pillow under the shoulder blade to raise the shoulder, so that the dislocation is eased by the stretching of the shoulder, or tie the arm to the neck and do not release it if no bad accident occurs, up to twenty days; then start the poultice again, if you see that it is needed, and adjust it, and let it be thus, until it is healed; and it is usually healed in twenty-eight days, or less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	Then the shoulder may be broken or widely separated in the middle, and one should not use force except through touch; then adjust the apparatus according to the shape of the fracture, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way you can; then apply flour from the mill with plenty of egg white over the area, and light cotton pads, and place a double linen cloth on top; then place a large, thin pillow, slightly larger than the shoulder, on top, and if there are any hairs underneath the shoulder, stuff them with cotton so that the pillow lies evenly; and then tightly bind it with a large bandage, so that the pillow does not move from its position, and check the binding every day; and whenever it loosens, tighten it again, and adjust the pillow if it has moved, and let the patient lie on his side; and the shoulder will be restored in 20 or 25 days. And when this number of days is complete, loosen it, and be sure, for it is not a bone that sets easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward, and not under the heart, then cut it off, and the bone, and do as we have said in the dislocation of the shoulder to soothe the hot abscess.Et se l’os tent desoz lou keur, et non pas avant, si fent de la maniere que nos avon dit; et se li espaule ne puet estre restoures, si covient li faire une chire ou une fente en l’espaule selonc la brisure, et le mettre dedens, et puis le brancher selonc la forme naturale, et le brancher fermement, et le deslie; et se li espaule fuert plus largement del keur qu’il ne devoit estre, si covient li faire une chire en l’espaule adons de la fente, si que li espaule siet igalment, et li faire brancher fermement, et le deslie; car il ne pouet estre restouree.
de la brisure dou pis	of the dislocation of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The feet are sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; they often break at the ends.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it declines downward, and the patient feels great pain, and lack of movement, and numbness, and sometimes he vomits blood, and the hair falls out from the broken bone, and he feels ill in that area.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is for the patient to lie on his back, and place a cushion between his shoulders, then press his shoulders together, and bring the ribs closer together with his hands, and carefully adjust the bone to its proper position; then apply plasters and poultices over the fracture site using a delicate salt or some other lightweight substance, and wrap it in a cloth, and tie it onto the broken bone so that it does not move; and re-wrap the ligament around the back, and tighten it gently, and check every hour if it has softened, and if so, tighten it; and if it needs to be loosened due to corrosion or itching at the site, or pain or an abscess, then do so quickly, loosen the ligament, remove the plaster, and treat according to the nature of the condition; then re-apply the plaster and tighten until healed.
de la brisure des costes	[treatment for a broken rib]
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that rib fractures occur only in the thick part near the back, and in the front near the chest, and they do not bend except because they are slippery; and it feels good when pressed on both sides.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is to reset the break evenly as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the ointment, and hold it in place with a splint if necessary.Et si li cheveimens ne vout pas aler sus li os, et qu’il soit brisiés, si met l’esguilez, et puis l’emplaustre, et li estele sus l’esguilez; et s’il ne vout aler sus li os, si met l’esguilez sus l’os, et l’estraint d’une estele, et met l’emplaustre sus l’estele.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of the ribs is bent inward, then the patient feels great pain and piercing, as with pleurisy, because the bone pricks the lung; and it also causes shortness of breath and vomiting a great quantity of blood, and it is a very serious condition, and the ancient physicians placed great importance on it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if there are those who say that one should administer foods that swell the belly in order to push the fracture out.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not agree that hot abscesses will not form if they have not formed already.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if he has come, then heal him.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one should apply cups to the area to draw out fluid, and this is reasonable; however, there is a risk that the cups might attract excess fluids due to the weakness of the tissue.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the area with warm, moist wool, and place tents between the ribs to create equal pressure all around, then it is cured by the treatment of pleurisy, with food and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hair does not grow on the broken bone, and there is doubt in the patient, then one must cut above the site of the break and insert an instrument to draw out the splinter; and then one must split the bone, and gently pull it out, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with ointments until it heals.And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure from the bone pointing through the skin, and there is doubt in the patient, then one must cut above the site of the break and insert an instrument to draw out the splinter; and then one must split the bone, and gently pull it out, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and treat it with ointments until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hot abscess comes, put on wet rags in rose oil, and apply it to the site; and while the site of the abscess is healing, lie carefully on the affected side, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	from the break in the neck
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a break in the neck bones, and it can bend; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, pay attention if you see his hands becoming soft, swollen, and numb, and he cannot move them or straighten them, and when you prick him with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is deadly in many cases, and if he is unable to move and feels pain when pressed or pricked, know that the joint of the bone is saved, and that the disease is healed, if one applies treatment.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar condition occurs in the spine of the back, and you want to know if he is healed or not, pay attention if his feet are swollen, and if the signs are in his hands, and there is flatulence and urination without willing it; and when he lies on his stomach, there is urination without willing it.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is lying on his back and he wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	You should know that it is deadly; therefore do not labor in its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident does not come to him, then the case is less serious.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you apply a hot poultice to the spine if there is an abscess, or rose oil, or the yolk of a new egg, until it is soothed; then apply one of the comforting and drying plasters, and bind it with a bandage, and instruct the patient to rest; and he must not sleep on the part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is exposed, it must be covered with a bandage; and remove the bone, then bring together the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a single stitch, then treat it with ointment in a bandage, until it is healed; and if there is broken bone, which is called the "bone of the cow", grab your left-hand little finger with your right hand, then apply the plaster and bandage it on, if you need to; then bind it, and if there is exposed bone, sew it up, remove it, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	It occasionally happens that the hip bone is fractured, and if it does, there will be some lessening at the top; and they hurt for a long time, and decline towards the sides, and the patient feels pain in the area, and there is swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that you extend your hand over it, so that you are on the break; and know which end of the bone is broken and its shape; and if the break is at the top only, then put it back in place, so that it is in its natural shape.Et s’il est au chief et a li parmain, si met cele qui es a li parmain a sa natureil figure, tant qu’ele soit au chief; et s’il est a li parmain soulement, si met cele qui est al chief a sa natureil figure, tant qu’ele soit a li parmain.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the break is long, or it declines inward, then let the patient lie on his stomach, so that the restoration of the break is prepared for him.Et s’il est dou lonc et decline au pardedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son costé tant que cele brisure te soit aparillie.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it even, then apply the ointment, and then place a wooden or leather splint on top, and hold the fracture steady so that it does not move; and apply the area below the ribs, until the color is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if painful abscesses arise, do not touch them until the painful abscesses are soothed, and apply what we have previously mentioned; then return to the restoration, and hold it as it should be, if there is no bad incident; and that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the shoulder dislocation
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The acromioclavicular joint is what is between the collarbone and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, it should be restored according to one of two methods. One method is that you take a stick of medium thickness, according to this shape:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	Tie both ends of the stick with two strings, and bend them upward, and press the patient down on a seat; then pour the broken arm over the stick, so that it comes to rest at the bottom, and press one curve of the stick inwards, and then bend it downward over some heavy object or by the minister extending it downward; then place the broken joint together in alignment with his hands, until the fracture returns to its proper position.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one supports the patient on his armpit and ties his hand to his neck; then command two ministers, one to hold what is above the fracture with his hands, and the other below to hold tight from underneath with one string, each pulling their respective ends.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more difficult, then constrict the ligament below the fracture, and above it, and extend each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.
