And if the fracture is close to the head of the shoulder, then you should put the ligament in the middle under the shoulder joint and the other towards the neck, under the fracture; and likewise, if the fracture is towards the neck, then it is necessary to put the ligament lightly without exertion, as long as the fracture is even on its location and on the neck; then put the fracture evenly as it should be, and constrict it, if no abscesses come about.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if a hot abscess comes, do not drain it until the 7th day, and put soft linen in ash and rose oil on the hot abscess until the hot abscess is soothed; then drain it, and the way to drain it is to put the ointment on the break, then assemble the arm on the shoulder, and put your hand on the shoulder or on the breast; and put the cloth, and drain on the shoulder, and on the arm, so that the arm is in its place, unless something moves it, or if the bone is moved.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone will move, use splints, and put on the break a splint wider and stronger than the others, and have between each splint 1 digit of space, and let each splint be as wide as it passes the break by 3 digits on each side; then drain over the splints, just as I said at the beginning of the chapter on the break, more strongly and less in moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the setting of the stars, and the restriction, as we have said, at the time that you restore the broken member, and you doubt the hot abscess, then leave it to heal until the seventh day, as we have said; then examine the bandage every three days so that itching or swelling does not come to the site, or the pus cannot reach the member because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If you follow these instructions, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, then do not remove the bandage until after three days or more, and let the patient sleep on his back, and place under the shoulder a pillow filled with wool of equal thickness, and examine every hour during the day or night to ensure that the figure of the broken member does not move, or the bandage become softened; then heal it through the power of medicine, and give him the food we mentioned earlier, in such a way that the food is at its most subtle; and when he begins to recover, let the food be thick.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to be wrapped for 40 days; and then one must loosen them and administer a bath and ointment medications to direct the area.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is ugly and swollen, it remains unloosed for 50 days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the break in the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm consists of two bones, which are called the "ulna" and the "radius." The ulna is smaller and located closer to the armpit, while the radius is larger and situated below the small bone. Sometimes only the large bone breaks, sometimes only the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, their restoration and healing is easier; but when the large bones are broken, healing is more difficult and painful than when they are broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is broken, one should gently straighten it and make it even.Se c’est li grans fosciles qui est soulement brisié, si doit on le poc estendre fort, et le mettre de la longueur que li petis foscile a; car il ne peut estre de la longueur du grans foscile, se il ne veult aler a piere.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the great artery, then it must be compressed more strongly; and extend it on a cushion, and hold the arm above the others, and the little fingers below the other fingers, and let the patient cross himself over his chest, and the cushion in front of him higher, so that he suffers no labor; then extend the assistant's upper arm to the part under his hand, or to the artery, and another assistant above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then put the needle in equally according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it is broken into pieces, let each be placed in its own position, and if any are displaced, hold the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then make an incision on the bone as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the breaking there is a wound, I have spoken of it in a particular chapter; let the cure be taken from there.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if at the beginning of the restoration, hot abscesses occur, then apply a dressing made of rosin oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and lay the dressing gently on top, until the hot abscesses are soothed.Et si li apostemes chaus ne voulent mie apaisier, si lie li drapeil subtilment et le piege soit fort, pour que li pus ne se puise pas en la veine.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerote and apply the plaster made from the powder of the mill with an egg, and then put on the splints, and let the splint for the fracture be a little stronger and a little wider than the others; and know that there should be six splints on the arm in various positions: whether the fracture is in one of the bones or in two; and apply more pressure over the fracture than elsewhere, and always less as you move away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the bandages over the fracture be soft and moist, and not hard or rough; and let the string used to apply pressure be made of flax, neither too thick nor too fine, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And then re-examine the limb and the bandage after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident happens to the limb, such as itching that comes to the limb, you should moisten the limb with warm water until the itching is relieved; and let the limb not be tightly bound but allowed to rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin the stretching again, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones separated, and similar things, then address them.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you perceive that the nutrients cannot reach the limb because it is too tight, then you must loosen it a little and leave it like that for several days, until the nutrients flow to it, and then tighten it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things we have said come to the patient, then do not release him until 20 days have passed.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or if it does not improve, then place your hands around his neck and keep his head level, and guard against movement and agitation, and let him sleep on his back; know that this broken neck will be healed in 30 days or 35 at most, and sometimes even in 20 days, depending on the different dispositions of the complexions.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and at the base of the fingers there are few fractures, and they come only with great force many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, then the patient should sit upright and straight in front of him equally; then put his hand on the stretched towel, and stretch the minister the broken bones, and put them even ministerially, so that they are well joined; and put the plaster and the poultices, if abscesses do not come, then put a cast according to the quantity of the place; and let it be wrapped in 1 linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the peritoneum around the abdomen of the plant, make a sphere of fabrics, and instruct the patient to hold it against his broken plant; then hold it with a long strip of fabric, and let the pad be of woolen cloth as large as the palm of your hand, and hold it, as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the furrow, you should put a pad on top and another underneath the plant, so that the hand is open and straight; then tie it all around the hand, and stop the bleeding between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture is in one of the fingers, whether it's the thumb, hold it straight and even as it should be; then hold it with the plant, and if you see, put a small straight pad to raise the fracture, and do not move it; and if the fracture is in the other fingers, such as the index or any other, hold it even, and tie it with the finger next to it; either tie them all together while holding it, which is better, or put a pad on top, as in the thumb; take care in the restoration and in the application of hot abscesses, and treat those that occur, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The thigh bone is often broken, and one can see this when it turns forward and backward; and its restoration is with one ligature above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extends each ligature to its part equally; and that is when the fracture is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the break is near the root of the thigh, then let one ligament be towards the armpit and the other under the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the knee, then let the ligament be over the knee, and make extension downward; then put the splint as long as his two hands, making the bone even with its natural position, then put on the ointment, and the bandage, unless an abscess comes there.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is a hot abscess, let him calm down and then return to your work and treatment; the ligature is made in such a way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap around the fracture a bandage of strong linen doubled into two or three layers, and thus keep the superfluous parts in check; then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the toe, and pass a long thread between the thigh and leg, below the knee, and have the end of the thread above; then return to the leg and thigh the bandage, then place splints on top of the fracture, and put a splint on the bone of the leg; then fill the space between the leg and thigh with soft rags to make the pressure even, then begin to tie tightly three turns or four on the fracture; and as you go higher over the fracture, lessen the pressure; then feel the two threads that you have passed between the leg and thigh, and tie three splints that are above, then return below to the end of the thread, so that you come by the foot; and make the pressure so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus so that no abscess or swelling or anything similar comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes, then loosen it, and treat what comes out of it as we have said many times before; and if there is a bone fragment protruding, then one must remove it if possible; and if not, then one must split the area and draw it out, and treat the wound as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And sometimes the thigh is broken like this when splints are put on, as in the shoulder and arm; nonetheless, the malady is not cured by this treatment.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the hip is restored within one day, or a little less or more, according to the variations of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the joint of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the joint of the knee there is little movement, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a fracture, or a perforation, and it affects everything, whether injured or not, and everyone feels it.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to put it back into place as it was before, with its bones aligned so that they can be set; then apply the plaster, and if necessary, use a round splint, and bind it as it should be, then follow all the instructions we have given for other fractures, such as hot abscess and similar conditions; then treat each accident as appropriate, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, one of which is properly called the "mustelz", and the other is called the "foscile". All injuries that occur in the arm also happen in the leg, and their treatment is the same as for the arm. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns completely inside out.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if only the small bones are broken, then it turns forward.And if the shinbone is broken, it turns backward. And if the thighbone is broken, it turns outward. And if both are broken, it turns inside out.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain and sees it clearly; and it turns inward.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	So bring about extension, and make it equal, and bind the joints equally. But still, if the fracture is ugly, and there are several pieces, then the extension should be less and gentler; and adjust it according to your skill.Et si li brisure est en la cuisse et ne va pas sus a la hanche, si n’est grant dolur, mais il n’y a point de mal, car on le puet aler et ruser, et selonc sa guerdon se met a la veine; et s’il y a mal, si est dolur, et il ne puet ruser; et se li esteles sont desaloiez, si ne puet aler.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, take two wooden splints which support the leg on both sides, and which are as long as the leg from the knee down to below; then wrap two bands around them, one above and one below, and tie the middle also, and at this time the leg will not decline to the right or left, and so it is well; and some administer a board as long as the leg, and it is of wood, and they place the leg upon it to prevent movement, and properly they do this in the fracture where there is pain; and move the leg each day to see if there is any hot abscess or other accident; and treat it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the fracture of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but at times there is a fracture of the bones of the foot and of the two bones, and there is only bruising in various positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if it happens that the bones of the foot are broken, and you see the bones sticking out above one another, then put that foot on the ground as if he wanted to walk, and then put your foot on top of his, where the bones are raised up; then press them until they return to their places. Then put the ointment and bandages on top, and place a small wooden board with two smooth sides underneath the belly of the foot, and then bind it tightly to the foot in a suitable manner, and then wrap clothes around it, and other things that you need.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three or four days have passed, loosen the bandage, for you will find the bones healed, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if any of the toes are broken, then set them as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint according to the length of the toe, and let it be a little wider, then place underneath the foot that board which I have mentioned, and tighten it appropriately; and if there are two or three, or more, broken, then place on top of each toe a splint according to its size, wrapped in one layer of linen, and tighten the board underneath the foot; and let the top of the board press firmly against the belly of the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, from what we have already said; and treat each case as it should be treated.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the finger
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bones of a woman's nature are broken, make her sit with her legs apart, then lean forward to her lower back, and hold her from behind; fill the opening of the nature with cotton wool, and insert as much as you can; then make the woman stand up, and gently lift her back little by little, and the cotton will pop out, until it reaches the entrance of the nature, and the bones will return with it; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and do this for seven days; then the break will be restored. If you wish, take a lamb's bladder, and tie a cane to the opening, and fill the entire bladder inside the nature; then blow into the cane strongly, until the bladder is inflated inside: the nature will return the broken bones; then it should be filled with cotton, and left like that for some days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the finger of man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the bone of the hip; and these breaks are not hidden from him who applies himself to this study and follows my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the breaks indicate in many ways the right way to restore them: understand this therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	When the penis is broken, take a goose's gullet and insert it into the penis; then wrap it tightly with cloth and leave it for three days or so, and it will heal quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for one who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, such as in the thigh or shoulder or similar, to be bled immediately, so that the bleeding we have described bears witness.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound bleeds, then apply vitriol again, if you have nothing else; then restart reducing the fracture in that same hour or day, if no abscesses appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses appear, then leave the reduction until the next day, as long as the abscesses are soothed; and do not touch them on the third or fourth day, because you would bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the uncovered chest, you should gently put it in place with your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not apparent to you to make it equal with your hands, then reset it with this instrument made of iron, which is seven or eight inches long, and its width depends on the size of the wound; and for this, the doctor needs to hold it with three or four fingers, depending on what he needs in each case of broken bone; and it should be smooth and slightly bent, so that it does not fold under pressure on the affected member during your work, and it should be thick at the front and wider from the middle forward, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And it is called «palainche», because the curved head of the bone should be placed upon the prominent end of the other bone; and it is bound in one place so that it may return to its original position and be even with the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is subtle and the instrument cannot hold the bone well, then you should chip away at the head of the bone so that the instrument can grip it.Et se li os ne puet rescevoir l’estrumens, si covient que tu tranches la chair qui le couvre, tant que li estrumens en ait possance; car il ne convient pas qu’il soit trop fort.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot reset the bone as we have said, then cut it with an appropriate instrument, such as an incisor or scissor, according to your ability; then remove what remains in the bone of sharpness and tiny shards.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	So do this until it is in its place, then soak the cloth in black wine vinegar, and use it to cleanse the wound if there is any pus or other discharge; do not apply cerate or anything else to the wound that might cause pus and corruption to form; then administer leeches after you have reset the bone, and leave the wound uncovered while wrapping the bandage around it according to the size of the wound; and be very careful not to restrict the wound with the bandage. And many fools have done this, causing death or corrosion in some cases; so make sure that the bandage is looser than others for dislocations.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	And if the wound is large and you fear that harm might come from it, as we have said, and there is pain in the area, then do not apply leeches to it; but wrap around the wound, instead of leeches, hard pieces of cloth, and tie them tightly.Et se li os n’est mie en son leu natureil, si covient que tu retorneis la dislocation et retorcheis li membres en son leu, et retorneis l’esguille sus la plaie, et laisse li drapeil tout descouverts; car il adut estre descouverts par journees et nuites, selonc que li chiés de l’aiutoire se guarisit.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days pus forming at the wound, then remove what you have placed over it completely, and apply an ointment that heals wounds, such as a four-drug ointment and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary to loosen the limb twice a day, in the morning and at evening, as long as it is sewn up and healing.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And one must prepare the limbs in such a way that the bowstring runs smoothly and lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if they go many days without healing, and it cannot be reset but keeps dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must probe the wound with a needle, and remove all the dislodged bone fragments that are causing the pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula or any other type of corruption occurs, you should treat it according to what he said in the chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when a bone is broken and open on the limb, such as the thigh or shoulder bone, and similar large bones, do not treat it at all, for many times death results from treatment; leave it be until it heals over, which may take 20 or 30 days; then treat the wound if you can, and if you cannot, leave it alone.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	of bruises that come over the weld
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We often come after the health of the fracture, especially when it is near the joint, and it is an ugly sight to see the shape of the limb; and by chance the limb cannot perform its natural functions.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if the swelling is fresh: have the physician administer astringent medicines, such as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcocolla, acacia, and similar others; crush one of these substances, or all together, and cook them in wine, egg white, or garlic; apply it to the wound as a poultice, and bind it on tightly for several days; then remove it and start another, until the nodule is removed. Or you can press it hard against a well-shaped piece of plaster; for the properties of plaster are such that it removes all inflammation from the limbs; if the nodule has turned to hardness like stone, and needs to be cut out, then scrape it away, and reveal the excess growth beneath; or have it removed by some scraper until it is gone and healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	of the limb that is weak after healing
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is healed and the limb remains weak and slender, it happens for many reasons: one reason is that it was bound too tightly, and not as it should have been; or because there were too many ligatures, and the nourishment could not reach the limb; or because of excess swelling; or because of excessive movement, not at the right time; or because there is little blood in his body, and so it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and soften the body, so that the blood is multiplied within him; and administer a bath to him, and give him joy and relaxation; then apply pitch to the limb, so that the pitch attracts to it greatly, and moisten often with warm water, so that the attraction runs into the limb; and restore it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	the limb bent after health
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are bent after restoration, and the broken bones appear, and the shape of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function; do not believe the fools who say that one must break the limb completely anew, and many fools have done this in our land; and these practices are blamed, and great harm comes from them, and even death; nevertheless, if the dislocations and torments are fresh, they should be moistened with warm water, or herbs that soften are cooked, such as leaves of marshmallow, and roots, and melilot, and similar medicines that soften the swelling; and you make a soft plaster, such as diaquilon well made, and you take the mucilage of marshmallow, and confit it with suet or fat of lamb, and make a plaster on it; or you take ripe figs, and crush them with colon dung, and similar medicines that soften the swelling.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And sometimes the joint is dislocated by continuously rubbing with wet hands for a long time.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be applied motion to the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the tortuosity is enlightened and hardened, like stone, and needs to be removed with iron, then it must be cut into subtly and lightly, up to the bone; and put poultice and study in the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation occurs in someone, one should immediately try to reset it without delay.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one delays, the place will become swollen, and if it is reset too soon, it can cause pain; many times it brings on swelling and other pains; nonetheless, when this happens, let the patient be bled, then let him rest until the abscesses are drained; then apply hot water and oil to the limb, then reset it gently, and treat each limb as the healing comes.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters on dislocations from the head to the feet.
des mandibules	of the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	Then the mandibles become dislocated and both dislocations are according to two ways: either they are slightly displaced from their place and made pliable, or they are completely dislocated and hang down towards the feet, and saliva flows from his mouth which he cannot hold in, nor can he close his mouth, and his tongue is wrapped around by speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it will return to its proper place through many remedies.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is complete, then you must reset it quickly and without hesitation; and in such a way that the assistant holds the head of the patient, and puts his thumb of one hand into the mouth at the root of the jaw, if the dislocation is on both sides; and let the other fingers be straight, in order to apply pressure equally; and instruct the patient to soften his jaws and move them about.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And she keeps an even pace until she returns to her place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the jaw is dislocated, especially if both jaws are affected, apply hot water and oil, and gently manipulate them until they return to their proper position; do not use force in this manipulation, as we have already instructed.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they are brought back into alignment and the mouth of the dislocation is closed well without softening, then place it on moistened cloths made with rose oil and wax, then tie it gently with soft ligatures. Let the patient sleep on his back, and let his head be supported between two cushions so that he does not move it to either side, nor strain to yawn, but take light food until the pains are relieved and the mandibles are healed. Then he may eat whatever he wishes lightly, and not strain to open his mouth to eat or drink as long as the mandible is well bound and healed.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two mandibles cannot be put back in place within an hour, and are not converted to their places, then fever and usual sores come, and by chance, intestinal problems, and by chance, vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is destructive; and many times, the person to whom it happens dies within eight days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceless cannot dislodge the constriction within the continuance of it and of the foot, and is dislodged sometimes by force, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	The restoration is that the patient lies on his back and extends his arms; then press the dislocation firmly with your palm, and it will return to place; then apply the plaster and bandage, and tie it tightly; and the shoulder joint near the neck cannot come out of alignment; if it does, and comes out again, reset it as we have said; then apply the plaster and bandage, and tie it firmly, and instruct the patient to rest until he is healed. Thus also is the shoulder joint reset when it has become dislocated from its place after being struck.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	You should know that the shoulder can be dislocated in three ways: one is at the bottom part of the axilla; the second is at the foot part; and by chance it dislocates at the top part, which rarely happens; and it does not dislocate behind the shoulder, nor inside for the nerves; and often it dislocates underneath toward the axilla, especially in those who have little flesh, but in those who have enough flesh, it dislocates with a pop and goes back with a pop.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance it happens to some men that they get a blow or fracture, and the shoulder swells with a hot abscess, and they think it is dislocated because of this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	Therefore, you must test it until you are certain, and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And you will know it is dislocated when it is down toward the axilla, and there will be a difference between the sick shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between them an obvious difference; and you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and underneath the axilla at the top of the shoulder, as if it were a hole; and the patient cannot bring their hand to their nose, nor move in any way; and also, if it is dislocated upward, it is not hidden, for you will see it obviously at the top; and this type of dislocation is not difficult to fix when it is new, or if the child is sick.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the method is for the assistant to lift the affected hand up, then place their fingers under the shoulder, and lift the joint forcefully upwards into position; while the assistant lifts the hand and extends it upward, then lowers it back down; this will bring quick relief.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come within a few days as we have said, then the patient should be bathed in warm water; and they should be given soothing and softening ointments, such as a decoction of alder and fenugreek and mallow in water, and then they should be wrapped up; then the patient should lie on their back, and a piece of woolen cloth that is neither too soft nor too hard should be placed underneath the shoulder, and then the minister should place their heel on the cloth, and gently lift the top of the shoulder, and pull the hand of the patient; and another minister should hold the head of the patient so that it does not move downward; in this way the shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that it is not returned according to this method, then you should have a man who is bigger than the patient stand upright by their side, and put their shoulder underneath the arm of the patient, and lift the cloth upward so that the patient hangs in the air; and another minister should pull the hand of the patient downward toward the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the dislocation is too light, one can use a heavy object with it, and the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And one can reset it in another way also: one takes a long rod and sticks it in the ground, so that the shoulder is as wide as the palm of a hand, but not too thick or too thin; then it is placed under the patient's shoulder, but there should be a cloth under it, and the patient must stand upright with his arm outstretched; then his hand is extended downward on the other side, and the joint will return to its place immediately; and if it does not return through all these things that we have said, then perform this cure: take a rod two feet long and four inches in diameter, which has a round head to fit into the socket according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	then bind it with soft cloth above the shoulder-blade so that the shoulder-blade does not hurt the patient; then put it under the shoulder of the patient, and stretch his arm out along the length of the brand, and bind the shoulder to the brand, and the arm at the tip of the hand; then let the arm hang down, and the body lean to the other side: the joint will return now.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, however it may be, you must put under the shoulder-blade a woolen ball the same size, then apply the prepared ointment of flour-mill powder, with incense and egg white, all over the shoulder and around, then stretch it under the shoulder-blade gently, and return the bandage over the ointment, and embrace the hand at his neck, and let the arm remain thus.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he eats little, until the member is healed, for he will heal faster; and then eat more after five or seven days, and move him; and if he is stiff and not softened, then he is healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has come out of place due to moisture or any other cause, one must administer cautery at three openings, as it is described in the chapter on cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this and the joint still dislocates after seven days, and the shoulder cannot be raised upstream, then know that the nerve at the head of the shoulder is torn or stretched or softened; and know that the joint will never be firmly set in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Dislocations that are towards the bottom, at the breasts, or behind, are made by pushing and stretching with the hands, and one should treat them until they are healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing, there is pain in the limb, and with movement, use the bath many times for the patient until the pain goes away and returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	about the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	You should know that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated by pins, and it returns by pins; and if it is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not reset, for one can see and feel it well, and it dislocates according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the sick neck with the healthy one, then you can see it clearly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is crooked, and cannot bend its arm or touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must reset it when the abscess has come out, for if the abscess comes out, then it is painful to reset it; and by chance it cannot be fully reset, especially when it is in the back; so it is worse than other dislocations, and causes more pain, and death may result.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the restoration is, when it can be reset, that you extend his hand with your two hands; and let his arms be spread out, and his hands bent according to the joint, inside and outside and around, and press the joint at his wrists together, or at the root of his palm, until it returns to its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, it returns when he bends his hand toward his hand, and presses from the root of the palm the joint that has been dislocated.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not want to return to its place, then it needs a strong extension; and while two ministers extend the arm, and hold it with their hands so that it does not move during this extension; then they turn the arm from each side, after having wrapped a long double cloth around it; and when you have joined the joint in his hand, then grease it with some oil to soften the joint, and then press it firmly into place, until it comes back into position. And when it is back in its place, put on a dry plaster with egg white, and hold it tightly in place, and keep the arm attached to the neck of the patient for several days, then loosen it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is firmly in place, he removes the poultice and leaves it; and if you see that the joint is not set well, then restart the poultice and bandage, and leave it for several days until it is firmly set; then release it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels stiffness after the joint is moved, and it does not move, then bathe and rub it well, and press until it is eased; or put a fat sheep's-skin on the joint, then leave it for one day and one night, then remove it, and have him enter the bath; and when he sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the skin back on, and enter the bath again; do this twice or three times until he is healed.
li dislocation de la main	dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand is healed, and its return is lighter than other joints. Nevertheless, it must be returned to its place gently, in the same hour that it was dislocated, so that the joint is swollen or an abscess forms.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	The method of moving it is to place the affected hand on a table and extend the fingers, then examine how the hand is placed so that the palm rests on the knuckle joint; press it until it returns to its proper position. It is necessary to check if it is back in the right position, then place the hand of the patient on a table with the palm down and extend and move the fingers.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then let the patient lie his hand on a table, and the operator should place his hand over the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it comes back into place now, that is good. If not, then strain it with soothing plasters and leave it as it is without manipulation.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after several days, then let the joint remain crooked; and it does no harm to the patient as long as his hand is relaxed, and he cannot grip anything at all: then know that the nerves are cut, or the arteries; there is nothing else to be done except straining with cautery below the injury, and by chance nothing else is needed.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	And when the hand is in place, then put on the plaster that we have mentioned, then squeeze and let go for .v. days, then loosen and leave it thus.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he cannot move it well, and there is any swelling, then wet it with warm water and rub it until it is healed.Et s’il advoit que li nerfs fussent copez, si puet il estraindre par cauterie, et frotter li sembables plasters sus le leu qu’il fut copez .
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the fingers of the handEt s’il advoit que li nerfs fussent copez, si puet il estraindre par cauterie, et frotter li sembables plasters sus le leu qu’il fut copez ..
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Sometimes the knuckles of the hand are dislocated on either side, sometimes at the back of the palm or on the inside; then you must pull the finger and push the dislocation towards the joint, and hold it there for a couple of days, then straighten it that same day; and do not ligature it, as we have said before, and loosen it at night, and make it move, and put a ligature on again during the day; and do this often until it is healed. Do the same also when it is dislocated in another place.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	dislocation of the shoulder blade from the back
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder blade or neck is dislocated, there is no treatment, for death hastens the disease.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the egestions jump out without any will, and he cannot hold them in, and many times a limb is paralyzed, either both legs or both arms, or one; and often there is a twitching in four parts; that which twitches at the back is called "gilbositez"; the cure is that you should investigate whether the gilbositez came from childhood: if it did not come from childhood, then there is no cure or healing for it.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from falling or blows or similar things, the ancient writers described at great length, but there is not much benefit in them all; but I have abbreviated it according to my understanding, and have devised instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that there is no cure or health in the gilbositet that comes to the front foot, and also in that which comes directly on both sides; but one can only be cured by that which comes directly on the back, as I said; and it is that the patient be stretched out on his face in one place evenly, and have a strap underneath him so that he does not twist; then put one tinder at the head in the ground, and another at the feet, and tie a cord under the sores of the malady, and another at the hips, and knees, and ankles; and two servants should hold the cords, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the tinders; and they should be tied firmly, the tinder as we have said, and the minister should put his palms on the spine, so that it recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this treatment, take a table three yards long, and lie on your side, and let the patient be on their side, and place the end of the table under the wall, then put the middle of the table on the spine; and let the patient put their feet on the other end of the table, and press hard, until it returns to its place; and if you see fit, do it while turning to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And you should insert two torches at the head of the patient, one yard in length, and towards the feet, two others; and between each torch, have an inch of space above and below; and let there be a hole in each torch, through which the string runs, and let the torches be firmly in the ground so they do not move; and between each pair of torches, let there be a turning torch, over which the strings turn, and let there be two small torches on each turning torch, one inch in length, for turning the string; and then tie the string that is among the pulleys to the turning string towards the head, and the other string towards the feet to the other turning string, and each of the ministers turns their string to all the string, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is equalized, then apply a desiccant plaster with plenty of egg white, and then toweling, and then the cast of a tablet three inches long, which colors the area of the hunchback and the healthy part of the spine, then bind it with a bandage, as we have said, and use a subtle cooling medicine on the patient until he is healed; and if anything comes to the surface at the end of the healing process, then one should administer softening and soothing medicines, with the cast that we have mentioned before; and sometimes they apply a piece of plaster, and sometimes the appearance comes to the surface on the back of the spine, and they think it is dislocation; and it is the bone that is exposed, so one must not be presumptuous about it: it might bring about death.
des dislocations de la hainche	of hip dislocations
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	You should know that only dislocations occur at the joints of the hip and shoulder, and not as with other joints; and the joint of the hip is dislocated according to four parts: inside and outside, front and back; and mostly inside, and less dislocated in front and back.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation within is that when one joins the diseased leg with the healthy one, it appears longer, and the diseased knee protrudes more than the healthy one, and the diseased person cannot bend their knee to the fire; and the place which is nearby is swollen with a hot abscess because the head of the thigh comes there.
