Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the signs of those who it afflicts are contrary to those before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the signs of those who it affects in front are that their leg is straight according to its length; nevertheless, they cannot bend their knee without pain, and if they want to walk, they cannot, and they retain their urine, and the veins swell, and when they walk, they walk over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the signs of those whom it affects behind are that they cannot bend or straighten their knee, and that leg is more crooked than the other, and the veins are softened, and the head of the thigh is at the place below the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remedies for this kind of dislocation are: if the dislocation is old and it persists according to its nature, then there is no treatment; and it must not be assumed that it will get better on its own.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And for the one whose dislocation is fresh, and it is of the four kinds of dislocations, you should quickly return the joint to its place, and stretch it in and out, and move it to the right and left; perhaps it will come back into place and require no other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this manner, you must prepare a strong minister and stretch the leg firmly with both hands, or with a strap tied around the knee; and another minister extends their hand above in such a way that they press their hands under their knees, then the leader of the strap tightens it around the thigh; and another pulls on the head of the strap; and they all pull up and down simultaneously so that the diseased person is lifted off the ground once and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This manner of extension is common to the four types, and if the dislocation has been reset, as we have said, that is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If not, then one must apply treatment to its appearance. When the dislocation is in the hip, one should lay the patient on his healthy side, then tie a bandage around the root of the thigh and the part below the armpit; then let the bandage go up towards the armpit and the underarm; then have another assistant grab his arms and squeeze the large part of the affected thigh and stretch it outwards: thus it will return to its place. This manner of dislocation is easier than others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot tighten it in the manner we have described, then one must tie the two feet of the patient together with a strong linen bandage around the heels and knees; then let the affected leg be extended two cubits more than the other, then hang from the end of a pole, with his arms two cubits above the ground; then command an assistant to grab the top of the thigh, and have another assistant hanging with the patient, who firmly grabs the thigh, for the joint will return quickly.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	And when the dislocation is healed, then the patient lies down, as we have said in the case of the hunchback, and he pulls the ligament tightly on the affected leg, and also on the foot; then he puts two torches, one at the head and one at the feet, then he inserts the torch between the buttocks of the patient in the middle of the body; and he wraps wet cloths around it so that it does not blister the patient, then he extends each limb towards him, and the surgeon holds the dislocation equal to his hand.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it relapses, that is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put him on the table and press him as we have said in the case of hunchbacks, and let the patient lie on his healthy side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocation is in front, it is necessary to extend the affected leg slowly, and according to what I have said; and have the assistant put his weight on the painful shoulder, then press with the other hand, and push the leg down towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And if the dislocation is healed, then one should not extend the patient downward or lift him up, but he should be as if his hip had been dislocated and was healed while lying on his back, as we have said before; and he should lie on his face, and the ligament extended as we have said, and they must press upon the joint on the table; and it will be all right when the patient extends his legs and they are equal; then adjust the buttocks, and apply the ointment, and bind it with a bandage so that the hip does not move; and rest for 3 or 4 days, then release him and apply the ointment again; and if you see that they are equal, then bind as before, and let him rest for 3 days; then release him and let him walk well until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee
Li genous est desaluez selonc .iij. manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	Knees are dislocated in three ways: that is, on the inside, on the outside, and behind; but they are not dislocated in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the sign is that you command the patient to bend his leg at his thigh, and if it doesn't stick to his thigh, you know that he is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit up straight, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and put his foot on your feet; then take his knee in your palms, and pull between your fingers, then bend the two sides of the knee gently; and another minister extends his foot, until the knee returns to its place, and the sign is that he sticks his leg to his thigh lightly; and put the plaster on, and let the leg air at the thigh, and bind them together strongly for three or four days, then loosen it; and the patient should not work at all, until the limb is healed.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the member is not at all, then administer a very strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until it is healed.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation of the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are sometimes dislocated, and sometimes fully dislocated, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is swollen, and it hurts when pressed on the affected part; the movements are light, and one should gently stretch it with their hands when it is only dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely healed, you should make the patient stand upright, and hold his leg firmly by the ankle; then draw the foot towards you with your right hand, and then with your left, twice each way; then stretch it upwards, and massage it well in that position; do this twice as we have said, stretching and drawing up the foot; if it pops back in, all is well; if not, repeat the process, for it will return; if it still does not return, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and push the peg firmly into the ground between his buttocks, and wind the cloth around so that he cannot move the patient; then hold the dislocation firmly with one hand, and another minister should stretch the leg at the knee, and the other minister should stretch the foot upwards with his hands or by the ankle; then stretch each minister evenly, and the peg should be pushed further between the patient's buttocks to hold him in place as he is stretched; then put the dislocation back into place with your hands, and another minister should hold the healthy leg from below, and the dislocation will return quickly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	And when it is at a point, then apply the plaster and bandages on top, and stretch it firmly, and bind the foot to the leg, and guard the nerves which are on the ankle behind, so that the ligatures are not too tight; then leave it for two or three days, and if the ligature becomes loose, then stretch it; then release it on the third or fourth day, and they should be able to walk by four days; and if he goes before that time, it is not safe that he will not relapse.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if painful abscesses arise, then you must soothe them as we have said elsewhere until they are healed.
des dois	of the arms
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the arms are dislocated, one should stretch them gently without force, and this is a minor matter.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocation is in any part of the hip or foot, then you should make the patient sit on a flat surface or table straight up, and put your foot on what is open from the joints, then press down on the foot firmly until it pops back into place; and when it is even, and there is nothing open, then put a board with two prongs under the sole of the foot, then stretch it firmly, and leave it for three days, then release it; and let him rest until he is healed.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wounds and dislocations together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When dislocation comes with a wound and you want to restore it, many patients die: so do not be presumptuous in the treatment if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for long, and if you are not kind and merciful and patient, nor bold; and at first use warm poultices for abscesses, and leave the patient in God's hand if you see no hope of recovery; but if you see hope, then reset the limb to its place, so that the hot abscesses may come out; and when the limb is in place, administer warm poultices to soothe the wound, as it should be, with drying ointments; and if there are fractures and small broken bones with the dislocation, set the bones and do as we have said for simple wounds; and beware of falling into fear, as I have said, for this will cause changes according to your Creator, and for the safety of your soul and body.
Amen	Amen
